<span
style="font-size:16.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;">**Title
of the Text**</span><span
style="font-size:16.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"></span>

<span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"> </span>

<span lang="JA"
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:Osaka\2212\7B49\5E45;mso-fareast-language:
JA">信心銘</span><span style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:
&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;mso-fareast-language:JA"></span>

<span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;">*Hsin-hsin
Ming*</span><span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;">
(Wade-Giles)</span>

<span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;">*Xinxin
Ming*</span><span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;">
(Pinyin) </span><span
style="font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;">Xin</span><span
style="font-size:10.0pt;
font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"><sup>4</sup></span><span
style="font-family:
&quot;Times New Roman&quot;">xin</span><span
style="font-size:10.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"><sup>1</sup></span><span
style="font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"> Ming</span><span
style="font-size:10.0pt;
font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"><sup>2</sup></span><span
style="font-size:14.0pt;
font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"></span>

<span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;">*Shinjinmei*</span><span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"> (or
*Shinjin no Mei*</span><span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;">)
(Japanese)</span>

<span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;">*Sinsim
Myong*</span><span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;">
(Korean)</span>

<span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;">Literally,
Believing Heart (Mind) Inscription or Faith-Heart (Mind)
Inscription</span>

<span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"> </span>

<span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;">**Various
Translations of the Title**</span><span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"></span>

<span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;">Different
Western and Eastern translators have rendered the title "*Hsin-hsin
Ming*</span><span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;">" in
different ways:</span>

<span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;">**1.**</span><span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"><span
style="mso-spacerun: yes">   </span><span style="color:black">Trust Mind
Inscription (Hae Kwang)</span></span>

<span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;">**2.**</span><span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"><span
style="mso-spacerun: yes">   </span>Inscription on Trust in the Mind
(Burton Watson)</span>

<span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;">**3.**</span><span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"><span
style="mso-spacerun: yes">   </span>Inscribed On the Believing Mind
(Daisetsu Teitarõ Suzuki)</span>

<span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;">**4.**</span><span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"><span
style="mso-spacerun: yes">   </span>On Believing in Mind (Daisetsu
Teitarõ Suzuki)</span>

<span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;">**5.**</span><span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"><span
style="mso-spacerun: yes">   </span>Words Inscribed on the Believing
Mind (Heinrich Dumoulin)</span>

<span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;">**6.**</span><span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"><span
style="mso-spacerun: yes">   </span>Verses On the Faith Mind (Richard B.
Clarke)</span>

<span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;">**7.**</span><span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"><span
style="mso-spacerun: yes">   </span>On Faith in Mind (Dusan
Pajin)</span>

<span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;">**8.**</span><span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"><span
style="mso-spacerun: yes">   </span>Faith in Mind (Sheng-yen)</span>

<span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;">**9.**</span><span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"><span
style="mso-spacerun: yes">   </span><span style="color:black">Trusting
In Mind (Hae Kwang)</span></span>

<span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;">**10.**</span><span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"> On
Trust in the Heart (Christmas Humphreys)</span>

<span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;">**11.**</span><span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"> Trust
in the Heart (Thomas Cleary)</span>

<span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;">**12.**</span><span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"> Poem
on the Trust in the Heart (Thomas Cleary)</span>

<span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;">**13.**</span><span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;">
Trusting In Mind (Stanley Lombardo)</span>

<span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;">**14.**</span><span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"> Song
of Trusting the Heart (translator unknown)</span>

<span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;">**15.**</span><span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"> A
Poetical Manuscript on Belief in the Mind (Katsuki Sekida)</span>

<span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;">**16.**</span><span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"> The
Mind of Absolute Trust (Stephen Mitchell)</span>

<span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;">**17.**</span><span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"> The
Mind of Absolute Trust (Robert F. Olson)</span>

<span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;">**18.**</span><span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"> The
Perfect Way (translator unknown)</span>

<span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"> </span>

<span
style="font-size:16.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;">**Author
of the Text**</span><span
style="font-size:16.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"></span>

<span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"> </span>

<span lang="JA"
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:Osaka\2212\7B49\5E45;mso-fareast-language:
JA">鑑智僧</span><span lang="ZH-TW" style="font-size:14.0pt;
font-family:&quot;Apple LiGothic Medium&quot;;color:black;mso-fareast-language:ZH-TW">璨</span><span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;mso-fareast-language:
JA"></span>

<span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;">*Chien-chih
Seng-ts'an*</span><span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;">
(Wade-Giles)</span>

<span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;">*Jianzhi
Sengcan*</span><span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;">
(Pinyin) </span><span
style="font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;">Jian</span><span
style="font-size:10.0pt;
font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"><sup>4</sup></span><span
style="font-family:
&quot;Times New Roman&quot;">zhi</span><span
style="font-size:10.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"><sup>4</sup></span><span
style="font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"> Seng</span><span
style="font-size:10.0pt;
font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"><sup>1</sup></span><span
style="font-family:
&quot;Times New Roman&quot;">can</span><span
style="font-size:10.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"><sup>4</sup></span><span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"></span>

<span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;">*Kanchi
Sõsan*</span><span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;">
(Japanese)</span>

<span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"> </span>

<span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;">"*Seng-ts'an*</span><span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;">" is
the Buddhist name of the author of the *Hsin-hsin Ming*</span><span
style="font-size:
14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;">, it means "Jewel of the
\[Buddhist\] Community." (Lit. "*Sangha*</span><span
style="font-size:14.0pt;
font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;">-jewel.")</span>

<span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;">"*Chien-chih*</span><span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;">" is an
honorary title given to *Seng-ts'an*</span><span
style="font-size:14.0pt;
font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"> after his death, by Emperor
*Hsüan-tsung*</span><span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;">
(*Gensõ*</span><span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;">) of
the *T'ang*</span><span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;">
dynasty. It means "Mirrorlike Wisdom."</span>

<span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"> </span>

<span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;">*Chien-chih
Seng-ts'an*</span><span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;">, the
third *Ch'an*</span><span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;">
patriarch in China, is also known as:</span>

<span style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;">•
*Ch'an*</span><span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"> master
*Seng-ts'an*</span><span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;">
(*Seng-ts'an Ch'an-shih*</span><span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;">;
*Sõsan Zenji*</span><span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;">
</span><span lang="JA"
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:Osaka\2212\7B49\5E45;
mso-fareast-language:JA">僧</span><span lang="ZH-TW"
style="font-size:14.0pt;
font-family:&quot;Apple LiGothic Medium&quot;;color:black;mso-fareast-language:ZH-TW">璨</span><span
lang="JA"
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:Osaka\2212\7B49\5E45;mso-fareast-language:
JA">禪師</span><span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;">)</span>

<span style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;">•
The third patriarch *Ch'an*</span><span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"> master
*Seng-ts'an*</span><span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;">
(*San-tsu Seng-ts'an Ch'an-shih*</span><span style="font-size:14.0pt;
font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;">; *Sanso Sõsan
Zenji*</span><span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;">
</span><span lang="JA"
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:Osaka\2212\7B49\5E45;mso-fareast-language:
JA">三祖僧</span><span lang="ZH-TW" style="font-size:14.0pt;
font-family:&quot;Apple LiGothic Medium&quot;;color:black;mso-fareast-language:ZH-TW">璨</span><span
lang="JA"
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:Osaka\2212\7B49\5E45;mso-fareast-language:
JA">禪師</span><span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;">)</span>

<span style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;">•
Great master *Chien-chih*</span><span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;">
(*Chien-chih Ta-shih*</span><span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;">;
*Kanchi Daishi*</span><span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;">
</span><span lang="JA"
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:Osaka\2212\7B49\5E45;mso-fareast-language:
JA">鑑智大師</span><span style="font-size:14.0pt;
font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;">)</span>

<span style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;">•
The third patriarch great master *Seng-ts'an*</span><span
style="font-size:14.0pt;
font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"> (*San-tsu Seng-ts'an
Ta-shih*</span><span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;">;
*Sanso Sõsan Daishi*</span><span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;">
</span><span lang="JA"
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:Osaka\2212\7B49\5E45;mso-fareast-language:
JA">三祖僧</span><span lang="ZH-TW" style="font-size:14.0pt;
font-family:&quot;Apple LiGothic Medium&quot;;color:black;mso-fareast-language:ZH-TW">璨</span><span
lang="JA"
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:Osaka\2212\7B49\5E45;mso-fareast-language:
JA">大師</span><span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;">)</span>

<span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"> </span>

<span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;">*Seng-ts'an*</span><span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"> is
Buddhist name of the third patriarch, his real name is unknown. The
following quotations contain information about *Chien-chih
Seng-ts'an*</span><span style="font-size:
14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;">, about which very
little is known:</span>

<span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"> </span>

<img src="img/image006.gif" width="138" height="204" /><span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;">**About
*Seng-ts'an***</span><span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"></span>

<span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;">Sõsan
*Sêng-ts'an*</span><span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;">. The
third patriarch in the lineage of the Chinese *Zen*</span><span
style="font-size:14.0pt;
font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"> Sect. In 592 he initiated
*Tao-hsin*</span><span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;">
(*Dõshin*</span><span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;">) into
the profound doctrines of *zen*</span><span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;">. He
died in 606. After his death, he was given the title of *Chien-chih
ch'an-shih*</span><span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;">
(*Kanchi-zenji*</span><span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;">) by
Emperor *Hsüan-tsung*</span><span style="font-size:14.0pt;
font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"> (*Gensõ*</span><span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;">) of
the *T'ang*</span><span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;">
(*Tõ*</span><span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;">)
Dynasty. The *Hsin-hsin-ming*</span><span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;">
(*Shinjimmei*</span><span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;">) was
written by him.</span>

<span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;">(*Japanese-English
Buddhist Dictionary*</span><span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;">
342)</span>

<span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"> </span>

<span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;">**About
*Seng-ts'an***</span><span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"></span>

<span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;">We have
little information about the life of the Third Patriarch. His birthplace
and birth date are unknown. According to the *Denko-roku*</span><span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"> ("The
Transmission of the Lamp"), written by Keizan Zenji (1268-1325), he was
a layman over forty years old suffering from leprosy when when he met
the Second Patriarch, Hui-k'o (Jap: Eka), for the first time in 551
<span class="smallcaps">c.e.</span> Being deeply impressed with this
layman's capacity for the Dharma, Hui-k'o shaved the Third Patriarch's
head and named him Seng-ts'an (Jewel of the Community). He was gradually
cured of his illness and, after they had been practicing together for
two years, Hui-k'o gave him the robe and bowl signifying the
transmission of the Dharma.</span>

<span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"><span
style="mso-tab-count:
1">         </span>Anticipating the persecution of Buddhists in China
prophesied by Bodhidharma, Hui-k'o ordered his successor to hide in the
mountains and not to teach. The Third Patriarch remained in seclusion at
Ch'ung-kung shan and Ssu-k'ung shan for over twenty-four years. He later
met the monk Tao-hsin and transmitted the Dharma to him. After that, the
Third Patriarch moved to Lo-fu shan, located northeast of Kung-tung
(Canton), for three years. Then <span style="color:black">he returned to
</span>Ch'ung-kung shan and died there in 606 <span
class="smallcaps">c.e.</span> It is said that he passed away standing
under a big tree with his palms together in *gassho*</span><span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;">.</span>

<span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;color:black">(*The
Eye That Never Sleeps*</span><span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;
color:black"> xv-xvi, Introduction of *Hakuyu Taizan Maezumi
Roshi*</span><span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;color:black">)</span>

<span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"> </span>

<span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;">**A
Brief History of *Seng-ts'an***</span><span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"></span>

<span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;">The
author of this Buddhist "hymn," Sengtsan (Sosan), the third (Chinese)
Zen patriarch from Dharma, the first Chinese and the twenty-eighth
Indian Zen patriarch, lived during the sixth century, dying in 606 A.D.
His place of origin is unknown. The conversion of Sengtsan at the hands
of Huike (Eka), the Second Patriarch, is recorded in the "Chuantenglu"
("Dentoroku"), Part 3:</span>

<span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"><span
style="mso-tab-count:
1">         </span>Sengtsan asked Huike, saying, "I am diseased: I
implore you to cleanse me of my sin". Huike said, "Bring me your sin and
I will cleanse you of it". Sengtsan thought for awhile; then said, "I
cannot get at it". Huike replied, "Then I have cleansed you of
it".</span>

<span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"><span
style="mso-tab-count:
1">         </span>Sengtsan realized, not simply in his mind, but in
every bone of his body, that his sinfulness was an illusion, one with
that of the illusion of self. As soon as we are aware of our
irresponsibility, all the cause of misbehaviour disappears in so far as
the cause, (the illusion of the self) is removed. If we have no self, it
cannot commit sin. Yet, it must be added, "I can't see how you and I,
who don't exist, should get to speaking here, and smoke our pipes, for
all the world like reality". (Stevenson, "Fables")</span>

<span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"><span
style="mso-tab-count:
1">         </span>He became the disciple of the Second Patriarch and
practiced austerities and led a life of devotion and poverty, receiving
the bowl and the robe, insignia of the transmission through Bodhidharma,
the First Patriarch (of China) of the Buddha Mind. At this time, one of
the periodic persecutions of Buddhism broke out. Sutras and images were
burned wholesale; monks and nuns were returned to the lay life. Sengtsan
wandered for fifteen years all over the country, avoiding persecution.
In 592, he met Taohsin (Doshin), who became the Fourth Patriarch. (R. H.
Blyth)</span>

<span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"> </span>

<span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;">**About
*Seng-ts'an***</span><span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"></span>

<span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;">Seng-ts'an
(Jap. Sõsan), d. 606?; the third patriarch (*soshigata*</span><span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;">) of
Ch'an (Zen) in China; the dharma successor (*hossu*</span><span
style="font-size:14.0pt;
font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;">) of Hui-k'o and the master of
Tao-hsin. Hardly any details are known of the life of the third
patriarch. There are, however, many legends about him and his meeting
with Hui-k'o. According to one of these legends Seng-ts'an was suffering
from leprosy when he met the second patriarch. Hui-k'o is supposed to
have encountered him with the words, "You're suffering from leprosy;
what could you want from me?" Seng-ts'an is supposed to have replied,
"Even if my body is sick, the heart-mind (*kokoro*</span><span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;">) of a
sick person is no different from your heart-mind." This convinced
Hui-k'o of the spiritual capacity of Seng-ts'an; he accepted him as a
student and later confirmed him as his dharma successor and the
thirtieth patriarch (third Chinese patriarch) in the lineage of Ch'an
(Zen), which begins with Shakyamuni Buddha.</span>

<span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"><span
style="mso-tab-count:
1">         </span>The incident that marked the "transmission from
heart-mind to heart-mind" (*ishin-denshin*</span><span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;">) from
Hui-k'o to Seng-ts'an is given in the *Denkõ-roku*</span><span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"> as
follows:</span>

<span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"><span
style="mso-tab-count:
1">         </span>The thirtieth patriarch Kanchi Daishi
\[*daishi*</span><span style="font-size:14.0pt;
font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;">, "great master"\] went for
instruction) to the twenty-ninth patriarch and asked, "The body of the
student is possessed by mortal illness. I beg you, master, wipe away my
sins."</span>

<span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"><span
style="mso-tab-count:
1">         </span>The patriarch \[Hui-k'o\] said, "Bring me your sins
here, and I'll wipe them away for you."</span>

<span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"><span
style="mso-tab-count:
1">         </span>The master \[Seng-ts'an\] sat in silence for a while,
the said, "Although I've looked for my sins, I can't find them."</span>

<span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"><span
style="mso-tab-count:
1">         </span>The patriarch said, "In that case I've already
thoroughly wiped away your sins. You should live in accordance with
Buddha, dharma, and *sangha*</span><span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;">"
\[*sambõ*</span><span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;">\].</span>

<span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"><span
style="mso-tab-count:
1">         </span>It is said that during the Buddhist persecution of
the year 574, Seng-ts'an had to feign mental illness in order to escape
execution, and that finally he went into hiding for ten years on Mount
Huan-kung. His mere presence there is said to have pacified the wild
tigers, which until that time had caused great fear among the local
people. The authorship of *Hsin-hsin-ming*</span><span style="font-size:
14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"> (Jap.
*Shinjinmei*</span><span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;">) is
attributed to Seng-ts'an. It is one of the earliest Ch'an writings. It
expounds Ch'an basic principles in poetic form and shows strong Taoist
influence. The *Hsin-hsin-ming*</span><span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"> begins
with a famous sentence, which comes up again and again in Ch'an (Zen)
literature (for instance, in example of the *Pi-yen-lu*</span><span
style="font-size:14.0pt;
font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;">): "The venerable way is not
difficult at all; it only abhors picking and choosing." In this early
Ch'an poem, the fusion, typical for later Ch'an (Zen), of the mutually
congenial teachings of Mahâyâna Buddhism and Taoism appears for the
first time.</span>

<span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;">(*The
Encyclopedia of Eastern Philosophy and Religion*</span><span
style="font-size:14.0pt;
font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"> 311)</span>

<span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"> </span>

<span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;">**About
*Seng-ts'an***</span><span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"></span>

<span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;">Next to
Hui-k'ê came Sêng-ts'an, who succeeded as the third patriarch. The
interview between master and disciple took place in this manner: A
layman of forty troubled with <span
style="mso-fareast-language:ZH-TW">*fêng-yang*</span></span><span
style="font-size:10.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;mso-fareast-language:
ZH-TW"><sup>1</sup></span><span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;
mso-fareast-language:ZH-TW"> according to the *Records*</span><span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;mso-fareast-language:
ZH-TW">, came to </span><span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;">Hui-k'ê
and asked:</span>

<span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"><span
style="mso-tab-count:
1">         </span>'I am suffering from <span
style="mso-fareast-language:ZH-TW">*fêng-yang*</span><span
style="mso-fareast-language:ZH-TW">; pray cleanse me of my
sins.'</span></span>

<span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;mso-fareast-language:
ZH-TW"><span style="mso-tab-count:1">         </span>'Bring your sins
here,' said </span><span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;">Hui-k'ê,
'and I will cleanse you of them.'</span>

<span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"><span
style="mso-tab-count:
1">         </span>The lay-disciple was silent for a while but finally
said, 'As I seek my sins, I find them unattainable.'</span>

<span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"><span
style="mso-tab-count:
1">         </span>'I have then finished cleansing you altogether. You
should thenceforth take refuge in the Buddha, Dharma, and Samgha
(Brotherhood), and abide therein.'</span>

<span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"><span
style="mso-tab-count:
1">         </span>'As I stand before you, O master,' asked Sêng-ts'an,
'I know that you belong to the Brotherhood, but pray tell me what are
the Buddha and the Dharma?'</span>

<span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"><span
style="mso-tab-count:
1">         </span>Replied the master: 'Mind is the Buddha, Mind is the
Dharma; and the Buddha and the Dharma are not two. The same is to be
said of the Brotherhood (*samgha*</span><span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;">).'<span
style="mso-fareast-language:ZH-TW"></span></span>

<span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"><span
style="mso-tab-count:
1">         </span>This satisfied the disciple, who now said, 'Today for
the first time I realize that sins are neither within nor without nor in
the middle; just as Mind is, so is the Buddha, so is the Dharma; they
are not two.'</span><span style="font-size:10.0pt;
font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"><sup>2</sup></span><span
style="font-size:14.0pt;
font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"></span>

<span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"><span
style="mso-tab-count:
1">         </span>He was then ordained by Hui-k'ê as a Buddhist monk,
and after this he fled from the world altogether, and nothing much of
his life is known. This was partly due to the persecution of Buddhism
carried on by the Emperor of the Chou dynasty. It was in the twelfth
year of K'ai-huan of the Sui dynasty (<span
class="smallcaps">a.d.</span> 592), that he found a disciple worthy to
be his sucessor. His name was Tao-hsin. He asked the master:</span>

<span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"><span
style="mso-tab-count:
1">         </span>'Pray show me the way to deliverance.'</span>

<span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"><span
style="mso-tab-count:
1">         </span>'Who has ever put you in bondage.'</span>

<span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"><span
style="mso-tab-count:
1">         </span>'Nobody,'</span>

<span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"><span
style="mso-tab-count:
1">         </span>'If so,' said the master, 'why should you ask for
deliverance?'</span>

<span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"><span
style="mso-tab-count:
1">         </span>This put the young novice on the way to final
enlightenment, which he attained after many years' study under the
master. When Sêng-ts'an thought that the time was ripe to consecrate him
as his successor in the faith, he handed him, as the token of the
rightful transmission of the Law, the robe which had come down from
Bodhidharma, the first patriarch of Zen in China. He died in <span
class="smallcaps">a.d.</span> 606. While much of his life is obscure,
his thought is gleaned from a metrical composition known as
*Hsin-hsin-ming*</span><span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;">, or
'Inscribed on the Believing Mind', which is one of the most valuable
contributions by the masters to the interpretation of Zen
teaching.</span>

<span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;">(*Essays
in Zen Buddhism – First Series*</span><span style="font-size:14.0pt;
font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"> 195-6)</span>

<span
style="font-size:10.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"><sup>1</sup></span><span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;">
Understood by some to be leprosy. (*Essays in Zen Buddhism – First
Series*</span><span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"> 195
n.1)</span>

<span
style="font-size:10.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"><sup>2</sup></span><span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"> In the
*Vimalakîrti*</span><span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;">,
chapter iii, 'The Disciples', we have the following: 'Do not worry about
the sins you have committed, O monks,' said Vimalakîrti. 'Why?' Because
sins are in their essence neither within nor without nor in the middle.
As the Buddha taught us, all things are defiled when Mind is defiled;
all things are pure when Mind is pure; and Mind is neither within nor
without nor in the middle. As is Mind, so are sins and defilements, so
are all things – they never transcend the suchness of truth.'</span>

<span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;">(*Essays
in Zen Buddhism – First Series*</span><span style="font-size:14.0pt;
font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"> 195 n.2)</span>

<span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"> </span>

<span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;">***Seng-ts'an***</span><span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;mso-fareast-language:
JA"> **in the** </span><span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;">***Transmission
of the Light***</span><span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;
mso-fareast-language:JA"></span>

<span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;">Translation
of <span style="mso-fareast-language:JA">chapter 31 of the
</span>*Transmission of the Light*</span><span
style="font-size:10.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;
color:black;mso-fareast-language:JA"><sup>1</sup></span><span
style="font-size:
14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;mso-fareast-language:JA">,
by Japanese <span style="color:black">Zen Master *Keizan
Jõkin*</span></span><span
style="font-size:10.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;color:black;mso-fareast-language:
JA"><sup>2</sup></span><span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;
color:black;mso-fareast-language:JA"> (1268-1325):</span>

<span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"> </span>

<span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;">Sengcan
said to the Zen master Huike, "I am riddled with sickness; please
absolve me of my sin." Huike said, "Bring me your sin and I will absolve
you." After a long pause, Sengcan said, "When I look for my sin I cannot
find it." Huike said, "I have absolved you. You should live by the
Buddha, the Teaching, and the Community."</span>

<span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"><span
style="mso-tab-count:
1">         </span>It is not known where Sengcan came from. When he
visited Zen master Huike, he was a layman over forty years of age. He
did not say his name, but came to the Zen master and asked for relief
from his illness, as told in the story.</span>

<span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"><span
style="mso-tab-count:
1">         </span>When Huike told him to live by the Buddha, the
Teaching, and the Community, Sengcan said, "I can see you are a monk, a
member of the Buddhist community; what are the Buddha and the Teaching?"
Huike said, "This mind is Buddha, this mind is the Teaching; the
Teaching and the Buddha are not separate. This is also true of the
Community."</span>

<span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"><span
style="mso-tab-count:
1">         </span>Sengcan said, "Today for the first time I have
realized that the essence of sin is not inside, not outside, not in
between. So it is also of mind. Buddha and the Teaching are not separate
either." Huike regarded him as having the capacity for the teching, so
he had him ordained as a monk and named him Sengcan, which means "Light
of the Religious Community." After this his sickness gradually
healed.</span>

<span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"><span
style="mso-tab-count:
1">         </span>Sengcan attended Huike for two years. Then Huike said
to him, "The great teacher Bodhidharma came here to China from India,
and gave me both the robe and the teaching. Now I entrust them to you."
He also said, "Although you have attained the teaching, for the time
being you should go into the mountains and not teach publicly. There
will be trouble in this country."</span>

<span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"><span
style="mso-tab-count:
1">         </span>Sengcan said, "Since you know about this, please give
me some instructions." Huike said. "It is not that I know – this is the
prediction given to Bodhidharma by Prajnatara, who said, 'Inside the
heart is auspicious, but outside is bad luck.' According to my
calculations, this prediction refers to your generation. Think about
these words and don't get caught up in worldly problems."</span>

<span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"><span
style="mso-tab-count:
1">         </span>After that Sengcan lived in seclusion in the
mountains for ten years. This was the time that the Martial Emperor of
the Wei dynasty persecuted the Buddhist religion. Because of this
Sengcan changed his appearance and stayed in the mountains, dwelling in
no fixed place.</span>

<span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"><span
style="mso-tab-count:
1">         </span>While in this condition Sengcan met the novice
Daoxin, who was to become his successor. He said to Daoxin, "After my
teacher transmitted Zen to me, he went to the big city and spent thirty
years there. Now that I have found you, why should I stay here?" Then we
went to another mountain, but later returned to his old abode. The local
people flocked to him and offered support. He gave extensive
explanations of the essence of mind for the people, then at a religious
meeting he died under a tree. His Poem on the Trust in the Heart was
recorded and circulates even today. Later he was given the title Master
of Mirrorlike Knowledge.</span>

<span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"><span
style="mso-tab-count:
1">         </span>The sickness plaguing him in his first meeting with
Huike was leprosy. But as he associated with the Zen master, his
sickness disappeared. There is nothing special about this story:
understanding that the nature of sin is ungraspable, he realized that
the nature of mind is originally pure. Thus he heard that the Buddha and
the Truth are not separate, that mind and reality are *thus*</span><span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;">. When
you really know the original mind, there is no difference in dying in
one place and being born in another – how much less could there be any
distinction of sin and virtue there! Thus the body-mind after all does
not exist; we are fundamentally free from skin, flesh, bones, and
marrow. Therefore his disease disappeared and his original mind
appeared.</span>

<span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"><span
style="mso-tab-count:
1">         </span>In expounding the essence of the teaching, Sengcan
said, "The supreme Way is without difficulty – it is only averse to
discrimination." In conclusion he said, "There is no way to talk about
it – it is not of the past, future, or present." Really there is no
inside or outside, no in between – what would you choose, what reject?
You cannot take, you cannot leave. Once you have no hate or love, you
are empty and clear. At no time do you lack, nothing is extra.</span>

<span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"><span
style="mso-tab-count:
1">         </span>Yet even so, investigate throughly to reach the point
of ungraspability, to arrive at the realm of ungraspability. Without
becoming nihilistic, not being like wood or stone, you should be able to
"strike space and make an echo, tie lightning to make a form." Carefully
observe the realm where there are no tracks or traces, yet don't hide
there. If you can be like this, even though "*that*</span><span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"> is not
the present phenomena, it is not within reach of ear or eye," you should
see without hindrance, you should comprehend without deviation.</span>

<span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"><span
style="mso-tab-count:
1">         </span>Can we add a discerning word to this story?</span>

<span
style="font-size:8.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"> </span>

<span
style="font-size:13.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"><span
style="mso-tab-count:
1">            </span>*Essential emptiness has no inside or outside
–*</span><span style="font-size:
13.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"></span>

<span
style="font-size:13.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"><span
style="mso-tab-count:
1">            </span>*Sin and virtue leave no traces
there.*</span><span style="font-size:13.0pt;
font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"></span>

<span
style="font-size:13.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"><span
style="mso-tab-count:
1">            </span>*Mind and Buddha are fundamentally* </span><span
style="font-size:13.0pt;
font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;">thus*;*</span><span
style="font-size:13.0pt;
font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"></span>

<span
style="font-size:13.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"><span
style="mso-tab-count:
1">            </span>*The Teaching and Community are
clear.*</span><span style="font-size:13.0pt;
font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"></span>

<span
style="font-size:8.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"> </span>

<span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;">(*Transmission
of Light*</span><span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;">
129-131 Sengcan)</span>

<span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"> </span>

<span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;">**Notes**</span><span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;color:black;mso-fareast-language:
JA"></span>

<span
style="font-size:10.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;color:black;mso-fareast-language:
JA"><sup>1</sup></span><span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;">
*Denkõroku*</span><span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;">
</span><span lang="JA"
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:Osaka\2212\7B49\5E45;
mso-fareast-language:JA">傳光</span><span lang="ZH-TW"
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Apple LiGothic Medium&quot;;mso-fareast-language:
ZH-TW">錄</span><span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;
mso-fareast-language:ZH-TW"><span style="mso-spacerun: yes">  
</span></span><span lang="JA"
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:Osaka\2212\7B49\5E45;
mso-fareast-language:JA">伝光録</span><span style="font-size:
14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"></span>

<span
style="font-size:10.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;color:black;mso-fareast-language:
JA"><sup>2</sup></span><span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;
color:black;mso-fareast-language:JA"> *Keizan Jõkin*</span><span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;color:black;mso-fareast-language:
JA"> </span><span lang="JA"
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:Osaka\2212\7B49\5E45;
color:black;mso-fareast-language:JA">瑩山紹瑾</span><span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"></span>

<span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"> </span>

<span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;">**Notes
on the Chinese Names and Terms Used in the Quotations**</span><span
style="font-size:14.0pt;
font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"></span>

<span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;">Chinese
ideograms of some of the Chinese terms used in the above
quotations:</span>

<span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;">**1.**</span><span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"> The
second patriarch Shen-kuang Hui-k'o (Shinkõ Eka, 487-593) (</span><span
lang="JA"
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:Osaka\2212\7B49\5E45;mso-fareast-language:
JA">神光慧可</span><span style="font-size:14.0pt;
font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;">).</span>

<span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;">**2.**</span><span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;">
*Ching-te Record of the Transmission of the Lamp*</span><span
style="font-size:14.0pt;
font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"> <span
style="mso-fareast-language:JA">(</span>*Ching-te<span
style="mso-fareast-language:JA"> Ch'uan-teng Lu</span>*</span><span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;mso-fareast-language:
JA">, </span><span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;">*Keitoku
Dentõroku*</span><span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"></span>

<span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"><span
style="mso-spacerun: yes">    </span></span><span lang="JA"
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:Osaka\2212\7B49\5E45;mso-fareast-language:
JA">景</span><span lang="ZH-TW"
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Apple LiGothic Medium&quot;;
color:black;mso-fareast-language:ZH-TW">德</span><span lang="JA"
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:Osaka\2212\7B49\5E45;mso-fareast-language:
JA">傳<span style="color:black">燈</span></span><span lang="ZH-TW"
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Apple LiGothic Medium&quot;;mso-fareast-language:
ZH-TW">錄</span><span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;
mso-fareast-language:ZH-TW"><span style="mso-spacerun: yes">  
</span></span><span lang="JA"
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:Osaka\2212\7B49\5E45;
mso-fareast-language:JA">景徳伝灯録</span><span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;">).</span>

<span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;">**3.**</span><span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"> The
meaning of <span
style="mso-fareast-language:ZH-TW">*feng-yang*</span><span
style="mso-fareast-language:ZH-TW"> (</span></span><span lang="JA"
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:Osaka\2212\7B49\5E45;mso-fareast-language:
JA">風恙</span><span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;
mso-fareast-language:ZH-TW">)</span><span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:
&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"> is not clear. Some authors think that it
is leprosy (lepra, or Hansen's disease). The related</span>

<span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"><span
style="mso-spacerun: yes">    </span>Chinese word *feng*</span><span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"> means
<span style="mso-fareast-language:ZH-TW">paralysis, leprosy, or
insanity. (See Ilza </span>Veith, *The Yellow Emperor's Classic of
Internal Medicine*</span><span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"> p.
49</span>

<span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"><span
style="mso-spacerun: yes">    </span>*feng*</span><span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;">
</span><span lang="JA"
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:Osaka\2212\7B49\5E45;mso-fareast-language:
JA">瘋</span><span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;">).</span>

<span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;">**4.**</span><span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;">
Tao-hsin (Dõshin </span><span lang="JA"
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:Osaka\2212\7B49\5E45;
mso-fareast-language:JA">道信</span><span style="font-size:14.0pt;
font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;">).</span>

<span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;">**5.**</span><span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"> The
title, Master of "Mirrorlike Wisdom" is "Chien-chih" (</span><span
lang="JA"
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:Osaka\2212\7B49\5E45;mso-fareast-language:
JA">鑑智</span><span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;">).</span>

<span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"> </span>

<span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;">**The
*Dharma***</span><span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;">
**Transmission From *Hui-k'o***</span><span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"> **to
*Seng-ts'an***</span><span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"></span>

<span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;">The
incident that marked the *Dharma*</span><span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;">
transmission from *Hui-k'o*</span><span style="font-size:14.0pt;
font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"> to *Seng-ts'an*</span><span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"> is
related in the <span style="mso-fareast-language:JA">chapter 31 of the
</span>*Transmission of the Light*</span><span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;
mso-fareast-language:JA"> (</span><span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:
&quot;Times New Roman&quot;">*Denkõroku*</span><span
style="font-size:14.0pt;
font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;">)<span
style="mso-fareast-language:JA">, by Japanese <span
style="color:black">Zen Master *Keizan Jõkin*</span><span
style="color:black"> (1268-1325), </span></span>as follows:</span>

<span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"> </span>

<span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;">\[The
interview between *Seng-ts'an*</span><span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"> and
master *Hui-k'o*</span><span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"> took
place in the following manner:\]</span>

<span lang="JA"
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:Osaka\2212\7B49\5E45;mso-fareast-language:
JA">弟子身纏風恙、請和尚懺罪。</span><span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"></span>

<span style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;">I
am riddled with sickness; please absolve me of my sin.</span>

<span lang="JA"
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:Osaka\2212\7B49\5E45;mso-fareast-language:
JA">將罪來、與汝懺。</span><span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;mso-fareast-language:
ZH-TW"></span>

<span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;">Bring
me your sin and I will absolve you.</span>

<span lang="JA"
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:Osaka\2212\7B49\5E45;mso-fareast-language:
JA">覓罪不可得。</span><span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"></span>

<span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;">When I
look for my sin I cannot find it.</span>

<span lang="JA"
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:Osaka\2212\7B49\5E45;mso-fareast-language:
JA">與汝懺罪竟。宜依佛法僧住。</span><span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"></span>

<span style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;">I
have absolved you. You should live by the Buddha, the Teaching, and the
Community.</span>

<span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"><span
style="mso-tab-count:
1">         </span>*Seng-ts'an*</span><span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"> asked
*Hui-k'o*</span><span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;">:</span>

<span lang="JA"
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:Osaka\2212\7B49\5E45;mso-fareast-language:
JA">今見和尚、已知是僧。未審何名佛、法。</span><span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;mso-fareast-language:
JA"></span>

<span style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;">I
can see you are a monk, a member of the Buddhist community; what are the
Buddha and the Teaching?</span>

<span lang="JA"
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:Osaka\2212\7B49\5E45;mso-fareast-language:
JA">是心是佛、是心是法、法佛無二、僧寶亦然。</span><span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;mso-fareast-language:
JA"></span>

<span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;">This
mind is Buddha, this mind is the Teaching; the Teaching and the Buddha
are not separate. This is also true of the Community.</span>

<span lang="JA"
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:Osaka\2212\7B49\5E45;mso-fareast-language:
JA">今日始知罪性不在内、不在外、不在中間、如其心然、佛法無二也。</span><span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"></span>

<span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;">Today
for the first time I have realized that the essence of sin is not
inside, not outside, not in between. So it is also of mind. Buddha and
the Teaching are not separate either.</span>

<span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;mso-fareast-language:
JA"><span style="mso-tab-count:1">         </span></span><span lang="JA"
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:Osaka\2212\7B49\5E45;mso-fareast-language:
JA">師深器之、即爲剃髪、云、是吾寶也。宜名僧</span><span lang="ZH-TW"
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Apple LiGothic Medium&quot;;
color:black;mso-fareast-language:ZH-TW">璨</span><span lang="JA"
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:Osaka\2212\7B49\5E45;mso-fareast-language:
JA">。</span><span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;
mso-fareast-language:JA"></span>

<span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"><span
style="mso-tab-count:
1">         </span>*Hui-k'o*</span><span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"> saw
that *Seng-ts'an*</span><span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;">'s
understanding is profound, he shaved his head and said: This is my
treasure. I name him *Seng-ts'an*</span><span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;">.</span>

<span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"><span
style="mso-tab-count:
1">         </span>*Seng-ts'an*</span><span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;">
attended *Hui-k'o*</span><span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"> for
two years. Then *Hui-k'o*</span><span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"> said
to him,</span>

<span lang="JA"
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:Osaka\2212\7B49\5E45;mso-fareast-language:
JA">菩提達磨遠自竺乾、以正法眼藏并信衣密付於吾、吾今授汝。汝當守護、無令斷</span><span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Apple LiGothic Medium&quot;">絕</span><span
lang="JA"
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:Osaka\2212\7B49\5E45;mso-fareast-language:
JA">。</span><span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;
mso-fareast-language:JA"></span>

<span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;">Bodhidharma
came here to China from India, and gave me both the robe and the
teaching. Now I entrust them to you.</span>

<span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;mso-fareast-language:
JA"><span style="mso-tab-count:1">         </span></span><span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;">Hui-k'o
gave him Bodhidharma's robe and bowl signifying the transmission of the
Dharma. He said:</span>

<span lang="JA"
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:Osaka\2212\7B49\5E45;mso-fareast-language:
JA">汝受吾教、宜處深山、未可行化、當有國難。</span><span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;mso-fareast-language:
JA"></span>

<span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;">Although
you have attained the teaching, for the time being you should go into
the mountains and not teach publicly. There will be trouble in this
country.</span>

<span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"><span
style="mso-tab-count:
1">         </span>*Seng-ts'an*</span><span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;">
said:</span>

<span lang="JA"
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:Osaka\2212\7B49\5E45;mso-fareast-language:
JA">師既預知、願垂示誨。</span><span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;mso-fareast-language:
JA"></span>

<span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;">Since
you know about this, please give me some instructions.</span>

<span lang="JA"
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:Osaka\2212\7B49\5E45;mso-fareast-language:
JA">非吾知也。斯乃達磨傳般若多羅懸記云、</span><span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:Osaka\2212\7B49\5E45">｢<span
lang="JA" style="mso-fareast-language:JA">心中雖吉外頭凶</span>｣<span
lang="JA"
style="mso-fareast-language:JA">是也。吾校年代、正在于汝。</span></span><span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;mso-fareast-language:
JA"></span>

<span lang="JA"
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:Osaka\2212\7B49\5E45;mso-fareast-language:
JA">汝當諦思前言、勿罹世難。然吾亦有宿累、今要酬之。善去善行、俟時傳付。師付囑已、即往</span><span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Apple LiGothic Medium&quot;">鄴</span><span
lang="JA"
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:Osaka\2212\7B49\5E45;mso-fareast-language:
JA">都、隨宜説法。</span><span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;mso-fareast-language:
JA"></span>

<span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;">It is
not that I know – this is the prediction given to
*Bodhidharma*</span><span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"> by
*Prajnatara*</span><span
style="font-size:10.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;color:black;mso-fareast-language:
JA"><sup>1</sup></span><span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;">, who
said, "Inside the heart is auspicious, but outside is bad luck."
According to my calculations, this prediction refers to your generation.
Think about these words and don't get caught up in worldly
problems.</span>

<span
style="font-size:10.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;color:black;mso-fareast-language:
JA"><sup>1</sup></span><span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"> The
27th Buddhist patriarch in India and *Bodhidharma*</span><span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;">'s
master *Prajnatara*</span><span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;">, his
name means "Pearl of Wisdom" (</span><span lang="JA"
style="font-size:14.0pt;
font-family:Osaka\2212\7B49\5E45;mso-fareast-language:JA">般若多羅</span><span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;">).</span>

<span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"> </span>

<span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;">**The
*Dharma***</span><span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;">
**Transmission From *Seng-ts'an***</span><span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"> **to
*Tao-hsin***</span><span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"></span>

<span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;">*Tao-hsin*</span><span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"> asked
*Seng-ts'an*</span><span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;">:</span>

<span lang="JA"
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:Osaka\2212\7B49\5E45;mso-fareast-language:
JA">願和尚慈悲、乞與解脱法門。</span><span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;mso-fareast-language:
JA"></span>

<span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;">Pray
show me the way to deliverance.</span>

<span lang="JA"
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:Osaka\2212\7B49\5E45;mso-fareast-language:
JA">誰縛汝。</span><span style="font-size:14.0pt;
font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;mso-fareast-language:JA"></span>

<span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;">Who has
ever put you in bondage?</span>

<span lang="JA"
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:Osaka\2212\7B49\5E45;mso-fareast-language:
JA">無人縛。</span><span style="font-size:14.0pt;
font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"></span>

<span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;">Nobody
has put me in bondage.<span
style="mso-fareast-language:JA"></span></span>

<span lang="JA"
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:Osaka\2212\7B49\5E45;mso-fareast-language:
JA">更何求解脱。</span><span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;mso-fareast-language:
JA"></span>

<span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;">If so,
why should you ask for deliverance?</span>

<span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;">With
these words, *Tao-hsin*</span><span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;">
attained his final enlightenment.</span>

<span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"> </span>

<span
style="font-size:16.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;">**Problem
of Authorship**</span><span
style="font-size:16.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"></span>

<span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"> </span>

<span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;">Although
the third patriarch *Seng-ts'an*</span><span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:
&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"> has historically been accepted as the
author of the *Hsin-hsin Ming*</span><span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;">,
contemporary scholarship doubts whether he was in fact the author. There
is no record that *Hui-k'o*</span><span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:
&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"> or *Seng-ts'an*</span><span
style="font-size:14.0pt;
font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"> ever wrote anything. The
expressions and idioms used in the work have caused certain scholars to
place the date of its composition in a later year.</span>

<span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"><span
style="mso-tab-count:
1">         </span>*Niu-t'ou Fa-jung*</span><span
style="font-size:10.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;color:black;mso-fareast-language:
JA"><sup>1</sup></span><span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"> (<span
style="color:black">594-657</span>), a disciple of
*Tao-hsin*</span><span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;">,
composed a poem called Mind Inscription</span><span
style="font-size:10.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;
color:black;mso-fareast-language:JA"><sup>2</sup></span><span
style="font-size:
14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"> (*Hsin
Ming*</span><span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;">) and
the similarity between the *Hsin-hsin Ming*</span><span
style="font-size:14.0pt;
font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"> and the *Hsin
Ming*</span><span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"> has
caused scholars to speculate that *Hsin-hsin Ming*</span><span
style="font-size:14.0pt;
font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"> was actually written after the
time of the sixth patriarch *Hui-neng*</span><span
style="font-size:10.0pt;font-family:
&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;color:black;mso-fareast-language:JA"><sup>3</sup></span><span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;">
(638-713), as an improved, condensed version of the Mind
Inscription.</span>

<span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"><span
style="mso-tab-count:
1">         </span>According to Japanese scholars *Nishitani
Keiji*</span><span style="font-size:14.0pt;
font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"> and *Yanagida
Seizan*</span><span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;">, the
*Hsin-hsin Ming*</span><span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"> was
composed in the eighth century, two centuries after
*Seng-ts'an*</span><span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"> (see
*Nishitani Keiji*</span><span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"> and
*Yanagida Seizan*</span><span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;">, eds.,
*Zenke Goroku*</span><span
style="font-size:10.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;color:black;mso-fareast-language:
JA"><sup>4</sup></span><span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;
mso-fareast-language:JA"> </span><span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:
&quot;Times New Roman&quot;">vol.2; Tõkyõ: Chikuma Shobõ, 1974, pp.
105-112). *Yanagida Seizan*</span><span style="font-size:14.0pt;
font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"> also suspects that the
*Hsin-hsin Ming*</span><span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"> is the
work of the fourth patriarch *Tao-hsin*</span><span
style="font-size:14.0pt;
font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"> (580-651). Chinese scholar
*Yin-shun*</span><span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"> shares
this opinion in his *Chung-kuo Ch'an-tsung Shih*</span><span
style="font-size:10.0pt;
font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;color:black;mso-fareast-language:JA"><sup>5</sup></span><span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;">, pp.
52-60.</span>

<span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"><span
style="mso-tab-count:
1">         </span>Some scholars also believe that the author of the
*Hsin-hsin Ming*</span><span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"> was
not *Seng-ts'an*</span><span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"> but
the fourth Ch'an patriarch *Tao-hsin*</span><span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;">. As
observed in most religious and spiritual traditions, putting down to
writing what one's master recited was a common practice. It is therefore
also possible, as some scholars suspect, that *Seng-ts'an*</span><span
style="font-size:
14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"> only recited the poem,
and it was later written by one of his disciples.</span>

<span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"> </span>

<span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;">**Notes**</span><span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"></span>

<span
style="font-size:10.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;color:black;mso-fareast-language:
JA"><sup>1</sup></span><span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;">
*Niu-t'ou Fa-jung*</span><span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"> (*Gozu
Hõyû*</span><span style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:
&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"> </span><span lang="JA"
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:
Osaka\2212\7B49\5E45;mso-fareast-language:JA">牛頭法融</span><span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;">)</span>

<span
style="font-size:10.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;color:black;mso-fareast-language:
JA"><sup>2</sup></span><span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"> *Hsin
Ming*</span><span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;">
(*Shinmei*</span><span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;">
</span><span lang="JA"
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:Osaka\2212\7B49\5E45;
mso-fareast-language:JA">心銘</span><span style="font-size:14.0pt;
font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;mso-fareast-language:JA">)</span><span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"></span>

<span
style="font-size:10.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;color:black;mso-fareast-language:
JA"><sup>3</sup></span><span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;">
*Hui-neng Ta-chien*</span><span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"> (*Enõ
Daikan*</span><span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;">
</span><span lang="JA"
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:Osaka\2212\7B49\5E45;
mso-fareast-language:JA">慧能大鑑</span><span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;">)</span>

<span
style="font-size:10.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;color:black;mso-fareast-language:
JA"><sup>4</sup></span><span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"> *Zenke
Goroku*</span><span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;">
(</span><span lang="JA"
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:Osaka\2212\7B49\5E45;
mso-fareast-language:JA">禅家語録</span><span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;mso-fareast-language:
JA">)</span><span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"></span>

<span
style="font-size:10.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;color:black;mso-fareast-language:
JA"><sup>5</sup></span><span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;">
*Chung-kuo Ch'an-tsung Shih*</span><span style="font-size:14.0pt;
font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"> (</span><span lang="JA"
style="font-size:14.0pt;
font-family:Osaka\2212\7B49\5E45;mso-fareast-language:JA">中国禅宗史</span><span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;mso-fareast-language:
JA">)</span><span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"></span>

<span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"> </span>

<span
style="font-size:16.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;">**Written
Sources of the Text**</span><span
style="font-size:16.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"></span>

<span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"> </span>

<span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;">There
were no separately published editions of the *Hsin-hsin
Ming*</span><span style="font-size:
14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;">. The classical source
of the *Hsin-hsin Ming*</span><span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"> is the
chapter 30 of the *Transmission of the Lamp*</span><span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;">. Full
title of this work is *Ching-te Record of the Transmission of the
Lamp*</span><span
style="font-size:10.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;color:black;mso-fareast-language:
JA"><sup>1</sup></span><span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"> and it
is found in the Japanese canon of Buddhist sûtras titled *Taishõ
Daizõkyõ*</span><span style="font-size:10.0pt;font-family:
&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;color:black;mso-fareast-language:JA"><sup>2</sup></span><span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;">,<span
style="mso-fareast-language:
JA"> </span>vol. 48, No. 2010.</span>

<span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"><span
style="mso-tab-count:
1">         </span>Two *Tun-huang*</span><span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;">
manuscripts</span><span
style="font-size:10.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;color:black;mso-fareast-language:
JA"><sup>3</sup></span><span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;">
containing the text of the *Hsin-hsin Ming*</span><span
style="font-size:
14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"> were discovered in 1926
(Pelliot 2104, 4638; Stein 4037, 5692). Presently, one of these
manuscripts is in Paris and the other in London. The manuscripts were
collated by *Kim Ku-Kyông*</span><span
style="font-size:10.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;color:black;mso-fareast-language:
JA"><sup>4</sup></span><span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"> in
1931 and later reprinted in the *Taishõ Shinshû Daizõkyõ*</span><span
style="font-size:10.0pt;font-family:
&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;color:black;mso-fareast-language:JA"><sup>5</sup></span><span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;">,
85.1283-1290. One of the manuscripts is the *Record of the Masters and
Disciples of the Lankâ*</span><span
style="font-size:10.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;color:black;mso-fareast-language:
JA"><sup>6</sup></span><span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"> which
contains historical information about the first Ch'an patriarchs
(Pelliot 3436, Stein 2054). There are minor variations between the
*Taishõ Daizõkyõ*</span><span style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:
&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"> version and the versions in the
*Tun-huang*</span><span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;">
manuscripts.</span>

<span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"><span
style="mso-tab-count:
1">         </span>In one of the *Tun-huang*</span><span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;">
manuscripts, the *Hsin-hsin Ming*</span><span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"> is
conjoined with another famous Ch'an poem, the Song of Realizing the
Way</span><span
style="font-size:10.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;color:black;mso-fareast-language:
JA"><sup>7</sup></span><span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"> <span
style="mso-fareast-language:JA">of Ch'an </span><span
style="color:black">master </span>*Yung-chieh Hsüan-chüeh*</span><span
style="font-size:
10.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;color:black;mso-fareast-language:JA"><sup>8</sup></span><span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"> (*Yõka
Genkaku*</span><span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;">,
655-713). This text also contains twenty-four verses of the <span
style="color:black">popular edition of the</span> book published and
circulated <span style="color:black">under the </span>title *Ch'an-men
Mi-yao-<span style="color:black;mso-fareast-language:
JA">chüeh</span>*</span><span
style="font-size:10.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;
color:black;mso-fareast-language:JA"><sup>9</sup></span><span
style="font-size:
14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"> (*Zenmon
Hiyõketsu*</span><span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;">)
(Pelliot 2104, 4638; Stein 4037, 5692). There is also a <span
style="color:black">popular edition of the poem, </span>with variant
characters and verses, titled *Faith-Mind Inscription of the Third
Patriarch of Sui Dynasty*</span><span
style="font-size:10.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;color:black;mso-fareast-language:
JA"><sup>10</sup></span><span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;">.</span>

<span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"> </span>

<span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;">**Notes**</span><span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"></span>

<span
style="font-size:10.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;color:black;mso-fareast-language:
JA"><sup>1</sup></span><span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;
mso-fareast-language:JA"> </span><span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:
&quot;Times New Roman&quot;">*Ching-te<span
style="mso-fareast-language:JA"> Ch'uan-teng Lu</span>*</span><span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;
mso-fareast-language:JA"> (</span><span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:
&quot;Times New Roman&quot;">*Keitoku Dentõroku*</span><span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;">
</span><span lang="JA"
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:Osaka\2212\7B49\5E45;mso-fareast-language:
JA">景</span><span lang="ZH-TW"
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Apple LiGothic Medium&quot;;
color:black;mso-fareast-language:ZH-TW">德</span><span lang="JA"
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:Osaka\2212\7B49\5E45;mso-fareast-language:
JA">傳<span style="color:black">燈</span></span><span lang="ZH-TW"
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Apple LiGothic Medium&quot;;mso-fareast-language:
ZH-TW">錄</span><span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;
mso-fareast-language:ZH-TW"><span style="mso-spacerun: yes">  
</span></span><span lang="JA"
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:Osaka\2212\7B49\5E45;
mso-fareast-language:JA">景徳伝灯録</span><span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;">)</span>

<span
style="font-size:10.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;color:black;mso-fareast-language:
JA"><sup>2</sup></span><span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;">
*Taishõ Daizõkyõ*</span><span style="font-size:14.0pt;
font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"> (</span><span lang="JA"
style="font-size:14.0pt;
font-family:Osaka\2212\7B49\5E45;mso-fareast-language:JA">大正大藏經</span><span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;mso-fareast-language:
JA"><span style="mso-spacerun: yes">   </span></span><span lang="JA"
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:Osaka\2212\7B49\5E45;mso-fareast-language:

font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;mso-fareast-language:JA">)</span><span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"></span>

<span
style="font-size:10.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;color:black;mso-fareast-language:
JA"><sup>3</sup></span><span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;">
*Tonkõhon*</span><span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;">
(</span><span lang="JA"
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:Osaka\2212\7B49\5E45;
mso-fareast-language:JA">敦煌本</span><span style="font-size:
14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;">)</span>

<span
style="font-size:10.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;color:black;mso-fareast-language:
JA"><sup>4</sup></span><span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;">
</span><span lang="JA"
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:Osaka\2212\7B49\5E45;
mso-fareast-language:JA">金九經</span><span style="font-size:

<span
style="font-size:10.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;color:black;mso-fareast-language:
