Osaka\2212\7B49\5E45;color:black;mso-fareast-language:JA">至道</span><span
style="font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;mso-fareast-language:JA"><span
style="mso-spacerun: yes">   </span></span><span style="font-size:
11.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"><sup>s</sup></span><span
style="font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;mso-fareast-language:JA">
</span><span lang="JA"
style="font-family:Osaka\2212\7B49\5E45;color:black;mso-fareast-language:
JA">大道</span><span style="font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;
color:black;mso-fareast-language:JA"><span style="mso-spacerun:
yes">   </span></span><span
style="font-size:11.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"><sup>t</sup></span><span
style="font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;color:black;mso-fareast-language:JA">
</span><span lang="JA"
style="font-family:Osaka\2212\7B49\5E45;mso-fareast-language:JA">正</span><span
style="font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;mso-fareast-language:JA"><span
style="mso-spacerun: yes">   </span></span><span style="font-size:
11.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"><sup>u</sup></span><span
style="font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;mso-fareast-language:JA">
</span><span lang="JA"
style="font-family:Osaka\2212\7B49\5E45;mso-fareast-language:JA">太虚</span><span
style="font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;color:black;mso-fareast-language:JA"><span
style="mso-spacerun: yes">   </span></span><span style="font-size:
11.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"><sup>v</sup></span><span
style="font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;color:black;mso-fareast-language:JA">
</span><span lang="JA"
style="font-family:Osaka\2212\7B49\5E45;mso-fareast-language:JA">如</span><span
style="font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;">\]</span><span
style="font-size:14.0pt;
font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"></span>

<span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"> </span>

<span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;">**II**</span><span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"></span>

<span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;">Stanza
5, and the last two lines of stanza 4 are important because they
introduce several terms and ideas of overall importance for the whole
text. First is grasping (*ch'u*</span><span
style="font-size:11.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"><sup>w</sup></span><span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;">, Skt.
*upadana*</span><span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;">).</span><span
style="font-size:10.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"><sup>14</sup></span><span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"> With
grasping and rejecting suchness cannot appear. The same goes for the
duality of "following conditions"</span><span style="font-size:11.0pt;
font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"><sup>x</sup></span><span
style="font-size:14.0pt;
font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"> and "dwelling in
emptiness"</span><span
style="font-size:11.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"><sup>y</sup></span><span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;">.
Conditions (*yüan*</span><span
style="font-size:11.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"><sup>z</sup></span><span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;">, Skt.
*pratyaya*</span><span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;">), or
conditioning factors, are mental activity and external objects. Not to
dwell in emptiness means that practice of meditation can become
one‑sided if attachment is developed for emptiness, peace and purity of
meditative absorption. This is a recurrent warning, in all schools of
Ch'an. That is why our text puts an accent on oneness
(*i‑chung*</span><span style="font-size:11.0pt;
font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"><sup>aa</sup></span><span
style="font-size:14.0pt;
font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;">), which is also the main
subject in stanzas 6 and 7. </span><span
style="font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;">\[</span><span
style="font-size:11.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"><sup>w</sup></span><span
style="font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"> </span><span lang="JA"
style="font-family:
Osaka\2212\7B49\5E45;mso-fareast-language:JA">取</span><span
style="font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;mso-fareast-language:JA"><span
style="mso-spacerun: yes">   </span></span><span style="font-size:
11.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"><sup>x</sup></span><span
style="font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;mso-fareast-language:JA">
</span><span lang="JA"
style="font-family:Osaka\2212\7B49\5E45;mso-fareast-language:JA">有<span
style="color:black">縁</span></span><span
style="font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"><span
style="mso-spacerun: yes">   </span></span><span style="font-size:
11.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"><sup>y</sup></span><span
style="font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;color:black;mso-fareast-language:JA">
</span><span lang="JA"
style="font-family:Osaka\2212\7B49\5E45;color:black;mso-fareast-language:
JA">住空忍</span><span style="font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;
mso-fareast-language:JA"><span style="mso-spacerun: yes">  
</span></span><span
style="font-size:11.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"><sup>z</sup></span><span
style="font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;mso-fareast-language:JA">
</span><span lang="JA"
style="font-family:Osaka\2212\7B49\5E45;color:black;mso-fareast-language:
JA">縁</span><span style="font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"><span
style="mso-spacerun: yes">   </span></span><span style="font-size:
11.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"><sup>aa</sup></span><span
style="font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;color:black;mso-fareast-language:JA">
</span><span lang="JA"
style="font-family:Osaka\2212\7B49\5E45;color:black;mso-fareast-language:
JA">一種</span><span
style="font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;">\]</span><span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"></span>

<span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"><span
style="mso-tab-count:
1">         </span>Stanzas 5 and 7 (in contrast to stanzas 9 and 14)
speak about emptiness (*k'ung*</span><span
style="font-size:11.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"><sup>ab</sup></span><span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;">) in
practice of meditation, which can become a pitfall. In stanzas 9 and 14
emptiness is considered from the *prajna*</span><span
style="font-size:14.0pt;
font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;">‑perspective, as an essential
trait of the world and connecting principle of all opposites, all
dualities. On the other hand, one should not dwell and abide in
emptiness during meditation (stanza 5). "When working on Zen, the worst
thing is to become attached to quietness, because this will unknowingly
cause you to be engrossed in dead stillness. Then you will develop an
inordinate fondness for quietness and at the same time an aversion for
activity of any kind''.</span><span style="font-size:10.0pt;
font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"><sup>15</sup></span><span
style="font-size:14.0pt;
font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"> Stanza 6 accentuates the
overcoming of duality between rest and motion which is a subtle
obstacle. "If one abandons deconcentration in order to seek
concentration, what he will attain is the deconcentration but not
concentration. If one turns back on impurity in order to get purity, he
will get impurity but not purity".</span><span
style="font-size:10.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"><sup>16</sup></span><span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"> It is
interesting to note the fourth line of stanza 7, which expresses that
emptiness (in *prajna*</span><span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;">‑sense)
is definitely out of reach from the *dhyana*</span><span
style="font-size:
14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;">‑perspective. This has
to do with the dynamics of meditation. If one seeks emptiness trying to
reach rest, he always seems one step behind, until he realizes that
emptiness is the common and connecting principle of rest and motion,
being and nothingness. </span><span
style="font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;">\[</span><span
style="font-size:11.0pt;
font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"><sup>ab</sup></span><span
style="font-family:
&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;color:black;mso-fareast-language:JA">
</span><span lang="JA"
style="font-family:Osaka\2212\7B49\5E45;mso-fareast-language:JA">空</span><span
style="font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;">\]</span><span
style="font-size:14.0pt;
font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"></span>

<span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"><span
style="mso-tab-count:
1">         </span>In *Hsin‑hsin Ming* </span><span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;">there
is no explicit mentioning of meditation. However, sections II and III
can be considered as "meditation sections". They contain admonitions on
correct meditation practice, its possible mistakes and pitfalls. Stanzas
8 and 10 speak of stopping the internal monologue and the related
thinking. Returning to the root and turning inward are related with such
stoppage – otherwise they would just be an introversion.</span>

<span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"> </span>

<span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;">**III**</span><span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"></span>

<span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;">The
first two lines of stanza 10 introduce two important technical
characters: *chen*</span><span
style="font-size:11.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"><sup>ac</sup></span><span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"> (which
also appears in stanza 18), meaning true, real, and *chien*</span><span
style="font-size:
11.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"><sup>ad</sup></span><span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;">,
meaning view (Skt. *drsti*</span><span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;">). The
course toward awakening is not related with a mind in search of new
truths. Such a search only multiplies (dual) views, leading to a road
without end. That is why the admonition "abstain from views" is given as
one of the main principles of the meditative *via negativa*</span><span
style="font-size:
14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;">. </span><span
style="font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;">\[</span><span
style="font-size:11.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"><sup>ac</sup></span><span
style="font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;color:black;mso-fareast-language:JA">
</span><span lang="JA"
style="font-family:Osaka\2212\7B49\5E45;mso-fareast-language:JA">眞</span><span
style="font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;mso-fareast-language:JA"><span
style="mso-spacerun: yes">   </span></span><span style="font-size:
11.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"><sup>ad</sup></span><span
style="font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;color:black;mso-fareast-language:JA">
</span><span lang="JA"
style="font-family:Osaka\2212\7B49\5E45;mso-fareast-language:JA">見</span><span
style="font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;">\]</span><span
style="font-size:14.0pt;
font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"></span>

<span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"><span
style="mso-tab-count:
1">         </span>Stanzas 11‑14 return to the themes of oneness and
duality. The first line of stanza 12 focuses oneness of mind, or
one‑mind (*i‑hsin*</span><span
style="font-size:11.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"><sup>ae</sup></span><span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;">, Skt.
*eka‑citta*</span><span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;">). We
find that *eka‑citta*</span><span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"> is
mentioned back at the time of Asanga, who speaks about it in the context
of the fifth perfection (*dhyana‑paramita*</span><span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:
&quot;Times New Roman&quot;">) of the *paramita‑yana*</span><span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;">.</span><span
style="font-size:10.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"><sup>17</sup></span><span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;">
</span><span
style="font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;">\[</span><span
style="font-size:11.0pt;
font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"><sup>ae</sup></span><span
style="font-family:
&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;color:black;mso-fareast-language:JA">
</span><span lang="JA"
style="font-family:Osaka\2212\7B49\5E45;mso-fareast-language:JA">一心</span><span
style="font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;">\]</span><span
style="font-size:14.0pt;
font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"></span>

<span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"><span
style="mso-tab-count:
1">         </span>One Mind is also mentioned in the
*Surangama*</span><span style="font-size:14.0pt;
font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"> as a doctrine which enables
one to overcome dualities, understand senses as a part of *bodhi,*
</span><span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;">and
attain imperturbability (*acala*</span><span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:
&quot;Times New Roman&quot;">).</span><span
style="font-size:10.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"><sup>18</sup></span><span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"> In
Chinese Buddhism the one‑mind concept is exposed by Hui‑ssu</span><span
style="font-size:11.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"><sup>af</sup></span><span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"> (sixth
century) in "The Method of Concentration and Insight", which belongs to
the T'ien‑t'ai</span><span
style="font-size:11.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"><sup>ag</sup></span><span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;">
school: "...All dharmas are but one mind. Therefore there is no
differentiation in itself, for differentiation is the one mind. As the
mind involves all functions, the one mind is differentiation. They are
always the same and always different".</span><span
style="font-size:10.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"><sup>19</sup></span><span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;">
</span><span
style="font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;">\[</span><span
style="font-size:11.0pt;
font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"><sup>af</sup></span><span
style="font-size:14.0pt;
font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"> </span><span lang="JA"
style="font-family:Osaka\2212\7B49\5E45;
mso-fareast-language:JA">慧思</span><span style="font-size:14.0pt;
font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"><span
style="mso-spacerun: yes">   </span></span><span
style="font-size:11.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"><sup>ag</sup></span><span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;">
</span><span lang="JA"
style="font-family:Osaka\2212\7B49\5E45;mso-fareast-language:JA">天台</span><span
style="font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;">\]</span><span
style="font-size:14.0pt;
font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"></span>

<span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"><span
style="mso-tab-count:
1">         </span>The one mind doctrine was especially elaborated in
the *Awakening of Faith in the Mahayana*</span><span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;">.</span><span
style="font-size:10.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"><sup>20</sup></span><span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"> Here,
one mind appears as suchness (*tathata*</span><span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:
&quot;Times New Roman&quot;">), in its pure form, and as
*samsara*</span><span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"> when
it falls under conditions. Fa‑tsang</span><span
style="font-size:11.0pt;font-family:
&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"><sup>ah</sup></span><span
style="font-size:14.0pt;
font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"> has written a commentary on
the *Awakening of Faith*</span><span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;">. For
him, one mind is the unchanging, undifferentiated, non‑dual basis of all
experience: deluded and awakened. </span><span
style="font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;">\[</span><span
style="font-size:11.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"><sup>ah</sup></span><span
style="font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;color:black;mso-fareast-language:JA">
</span><span lang="JA"
style="font-family:Osaka\2212\7B49\5E45;mso-fareast-language:JA">法藏</span><span
style="font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;">\]</span><span
style="font-size:14.0pt;
font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"></span>

<span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"><span
style="mso-tab-count:
1">         </span>In *Hsin‑hsin Ming*</span><span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"> one
mind is considered in a meditative context (rather than as a
metaphysical concept). It is a state of mind free of duality.</span>

<span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"> </span>

<span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;">**IV**</span><span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"></span>

<span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;">In the
second line</span><span
style="font-size:10.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"><sup>21</sup></span><span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"> in
stanza 17 we encounter the character *t'i*</span><span
style="font-size:11.0pt;
font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"><sup>ai</sup></span><span
style="font-size:14.0pt;
font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"> (essence, substance) which is
usually paired with *yung*</span><span
style="font-size:11.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"><sup>aj</sup></span><span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;">
(function, application). It is an important concept in Buddhism, and
other schools of Chinese philosophy. The character *yung*</span><span
style="font-size:
14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"> appears also in our
text (in Stanzas 18 and 21), but the context suggests a colloquial
rendering: "to use". Peculiar for our text is that (in stanza 12) it
focuses blame (*chin*</span><span
style="font-size:11.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"><sup>ak</sup></span><span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;">) as a
factor that binds mind to things and arising (*cheng*</span><span
style="font-size:11.0pt;
font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"><sup>al</sup></span><span
style="font-size:14.0pt;
font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;">). This relatedness of the
subject and object is underlined in verse 13. </span><span
style="font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;">\[</span><span
style="font-size:11.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"><sup>ai</sup></span><span
style="font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"> </span><span lang="JA"
style="font-family:
Osaka\2212\7B49\5E45;mso-fareast-language:JA">體</span><span
style="font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;mso-fareast-language:JA"><span
style="mso-spacerun: yes">   </span></span><span style="font-size:
11.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"><sup>aj</sup></span><span
style="font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;mso-fareast-language:JA">
</span><span lang="JA"
style="font-family:Osaka\2212\7B49\5E45;mso-fareast-language:JA">用</span><span
style="font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;color:black;mso-fareast-language:JA"><span
style="mso-spacerun: yes">   </span></span><span style="font-size:
11.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"><sup>ak</sup></span><span
style="font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;color:black;mso-fareast-language:JA">
</span><span lang="JA"
style="font-family:Osaka\2212\7B49\5E45;mso-fareast-language:JA">咎</span><span
style="font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;mso-fareast-language:JA"><span
style="mso-spacerun: yes">   </span></span><span style="font-size:
11.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"><sup>al</sup></span><span
style="font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;mso-fareast-language:JA">
</span><span lang="JA"
style="font-family:Osaka\2212\7B49\5E45;mso-fareast-language:JA">正</span><span
style="font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;">\]</span><span
style="font-size:14.0pt;
font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"></span>

<span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"><span
style="mso-tab-count:
1">         </span>In order to avoid duality, *Hsin‑hsin
Ming*</span><span style="font-size:14.0pt;
font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"> once more (in stanza 14)
focuses emptiness as origin of both. Now comes the second stage of
cultivating the mind: it consists in applying (*yung*</span><span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;">) which
is now changed through this "meeting" with *t'i*</span><span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;">. This
means that *yung*</span><span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"> itself
would be different after its "meeting" with *t'i*</span><span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"> (the
"meeting" is expressed by the "one‑mind"). That is, *yung*</span><span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"> is
changed when mind understands its relation with things (*fa*</span><span
style="font-size:
11.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"><sup>am</sup></span><span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"> –
Skt*. dharma*</span><span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;">) – how
is it influenced by things, and how it influences things. Then the mind
is free from things, as well as from its previous *yung*</span><span
style="font-size:
14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"> (function,
application); it now functions in the world, but is not influenced and
affected by the world. The new functioning in the world is exposed in
part IV (stanzas 15‑18) of the *Hsin‑hsin Ming*</span><span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:
&quot;Times New Roman&quot;">; there we find what is, and what is not
peculiar to such free functioning. </span><span
style="font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;">\[</span><span
style="font-size:11.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"><sup>am</sup></span><span
style="font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"> </span><span lang="JA"
style="font-family:
Osaka\2212\7B49\5E45;mso-fareast-language:JA">法</span><span
style="font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;mso-fareast-language:JA">\]</span><span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"></span>

<span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"><span
style="mso-tab-count:
1">         </span>In the third line of stanza 17 we encounter a Taoist
maxim of according with *tao*</span><span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;">, but
we should give it a Buddhist reading: accord your nature with the way
(*tao*</span><span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;">), i.e.
accord with the Buddhist path (Skt. *marga*</span><span
style="font-size:14.0pt;
font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;">).</span>

<span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"> </span>

<span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;">**V**</span><span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"></span>

<span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;">The
fifth part opens introducing the One‑vehicle (*i‑ch'eng*</span><span
style="font-size:11.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"><sup>an</sup></span><span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;">, Skt.
*eka‑yana*</span><span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;">).</span><span
style="font-size:10.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"><sup>22</sup></span><span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;">
</span><span
style="font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;">\[</span><span
style="font-size:11.0pt;
font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"><sup>an</sup></span><span
style="font-family:
&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"> </span><span lang="JA"
style="font-family:Osaka\2212\7B49\5E45;
color:black;mso-fareast-language:JA">一乘</span><span
style="font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;mso-fareast-language:JA">\]</span><span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"></span>

<span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"><span
style="mso-tab-count:
1">         </span>In China we encounter the subject of One vehicle
(*i‑ch'eng*</span><span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;">) in
the Hua‑yen</span><span
style="font-size:11.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"><sup>ao</sup></span><span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;">
school. As in other teachings in that school, it calls upon the
authority of the *Avatamsaka Sutra*</span><span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;">.
However, here we have an interpretation differing from Mahayana. In
Fa‑tsang's *Treatise on the Golden Lion*</span><span
style="font-size:14.0pt;
font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"> we find an exposition of
various schools and Buddhist doctrines in a five‑level gradation. The
Hinayana doctrine includes all Theravada schools, the initial doctrine
of Mahayana includes Madhyamaka and Yogacara, the final doctrine of
Mahayana is given by the T'ien‑t'ai</span><span
style="font-size:11.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"><sup>ap</sup></span><span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;">
school, the Mahayana doctrine of sudden awakening is given by Ch'an, and
the Yuan (rounded, complete, all‑inclusive) doctrine (*yuan
chiao*</span><span
style="font-size:11.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"><sup>aq</sup></span><span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;">) of
the One vehicle is given by the Hua‑yen school. What is this
all‑inclusive teaching of the One vehicle? "When the feelings have been
eliminated and true substance (*t'i*</span><span
style="font-size:11.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"><sup>ar</sup></span><span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;">)
revealed, all becomes an undifferentiated mass. Great functions
(*yung*</span><span
style="font-size:11.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"><sup>as</sup></span><span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;">) arise
in abundance, and whatever it does is real (or absolute,
*chen*</span><span
style="font-size:11.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"><sup>at</sup></span><span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;">). The
myriad manifestations, despite their variety, interfuse without
disarray. The all is the one, for both are similar, being empty in
nature. And the one is the all for cause and effect clearly take course.
In their power and functions each implies the other. They spread out and
roll up freely. This is called the all‑inclusive doctrine of the One
vehicle" (compare slight variations in translations of this
passage—because of its importance it was quoted by various
authors).</span><span
style="font-size:10.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"><sup>23</sup></span><span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;">
</span><span
style="font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;">\[</span><span
style="font-size:11.0pt;
font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"><sup>ao</sup></span><span
style="font-family:
&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"> </span><span lang="JA"
style="font-family:Osaka\2212\7B49\5E45;
mso-fareast-language:JA">華嚴</span><span
style="font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;
mso-fareast-language:JA"><span style="mso-spacerun: yes">  
</span></span><span
style="font-size:11.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"><sup>ap</sup></span><span
style="font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;mso-fareast-language:JA">
</span><span lang="JA"
style="font-family:Osaka\2212\7B49\5E45;mso-fareast-language:JA">天台</span><span
style="font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;color:black;mso-fareast-language:JA"><span
style="mso-spacerun: yes">   </span></span><span style="font-size:
11.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"><sup>aq</sup></span><span
style="font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;color:black;mso-fareast-language:JA">
</span><span lang="JA"
style="font-family:Osaka\2212\7B49\5E45;color:black;mso-fareast-language:
JA">圓教</span><span style="font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;
mso-fareast-language:JA"><span style="mso-spacerun: yes">  
</span></span><span
style="font-size:11.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"><sup>ar</sup></span><span
style="font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;mso-fareast-language:JA">
</span><span lang="JA"
style="font-family:Osaka\2212\7B49\5E45;mso-fareast-language:JA">體</span><span
style="font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;mso-fareast-language:JA"><span
style="mso-spacerun: yes">   </span></span><span style="font-size:
11.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"><sup>as</sup></span><span
style="font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;color:black;mso-fareast-language:JA">
</span><span lang="JA"
style="font-family:Osaka\2212\7B49\5E45;mso-fareast-language:JA">用</span><span
style="font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;mso-fareast-language:JA"><span
style="mso-spacerun: yes">   </span></span><span style="font-size:
11.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"><sup>at</sup></span><span
style="font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;mso-fareast-language:JA">
</span><span lang="JA"
style="font-family:Osaka\2212\7B49\5E45;mso-fareast-language:JA">眞</span><span
style="font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;">\]</span><span
style="font-size:14.0pt;
font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"></span>

<span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"><span
style="mso-tab-count:
1">         </span>Now, how does this Hua‑yen understanding of the One
vehicle stand in relation to *Hsin‑hsin Ming*</span><span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;">?</span>

<span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"><span
style="mso-tab-count:
1">         </span>We find this "one is all, all is one"</span><span
style="font-size:11.0pt;
font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"><sup>au</sup></span><span
style="font-size:14.0pt;
font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"> principle, and the Hua‑yen
teaching of mutual penetration and identity, in stanzas 33, 34, and 35.
Therefore, the One vehicle in *Hsin‑hsin Ming*</span><span
style="font-size:14.0pt;
font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"> is open toward six
sense‑objects (*lu*</span><span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;">
*chan*</span><span
style="font-size:11.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"><sup>av</sup></span><span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;">, Skt.
*sad guna*</span><span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;">), six
qualities (or "six dusts"), that appear in the conjunction of objects
and sense organs, including reason. Perhaps, it is the "dust" which was
supposed to be wiped from the "bright mirror of the mind" in the verse
by Shen‑hsiu</span><span
style="font-size:11.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"><sup>aw</sup></span><span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;">
(composed in competition for the successor of the fifth patriarch of the
Ch'an school), while Hui‑neng</span><span
style="font-size:11.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"><sup>ax</sup></span><span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"> said
that Buddha‑nature is forever pure and cannot be defiled by "dust".
</span><span
style="font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;">\[</span><span
style="font-size:11.0pt;
font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"><sup>au</sup></span><span
style="font-family:
&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"> </span><span lang="JA"
style="font-family:Osaka\2212\7B49\5E45;
color:black;mso-fareast-language:JA">一即一切、一切即一</span><span
style="font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;mso-fareast-language:JA"><span
style="mso-spacerun: yes">   </span></span><span style="font-size:
11.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"><sup>av</sup></span><span
style="font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;mso-fareast-language:JA">
</span><span lang="JA"
style="font-family:Osaka\2212\7B49\5E45;color:black;mso-fareast-language:
JA">六塵</span><span style="font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;
color:black;mso-fareast-language:JA"><span style="mso-spacerun:
yes">   </span></span><span
style="font-size:11.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"><sup>aw</sup></span><span
style="font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;color:black;mso-fareast-language:JA">
</span><span lang="JA"
style="font-family:Osaka\2212\7B49\5E45;mso-fareast-language:JA">神秀</span><span
style="font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;mso-fareast-language:JA"><span
style="mso-spacerun: yes">   </span></span><span style="font-size:
11.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"><sup>ax</sup></span><span
style="font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;mso-fareast-language:JA">
</span><span lang="JA"
style="font-family:Osaka\2212\7B49\5E45;mso-fareast-language:JA">慧能</span><span
style="font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;">\]</span><span
style="font-size:14.0pt;
font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"></span>

<span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"><span
style="mso-tab-count:
1">         </span>The integrative, monistic standpoint—similar to
Hua‑yen—is obvious from the third and fourth lines of stanza 19. This is
where the One vehicle and the one mind doctrine meet, because one mind
has two aspects: one is suchness (seen in perfect awakeness), the other
is origination and cessation with six sense‑objects. </span>

<span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"><span
style="mso-tab-count:
1">         </span>Stanza 21 speaks of possible mistakes related with
meditative practice. One can find similar instructions in earlier texts,
as in the *Surangama Sutra*</span><span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;">.
*Surangama*</span><span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"> and
*Hsin‑hsin Ming* </span><span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;">are
cautious and give warnings against the possible misuse of meditative
process. With the first two lines of stanza 21 compare two lines from
*Surangama*</span><span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;">:</span>

<span
style="font-size:8.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"> </span>

<span
style="font-size:13.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"><span
style="mso-tab-count:
3">                                    </span>*If mind be set on
searching for the mind, that which*</span><span
style="font-size:13.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"></span>

<span
style="font-size:13.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"><span
style="mso-tab-count:
3">                                    </span>*At heart is not illusion,
becomes illusory.*</span><span style="font-size:10.0pt;
font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"><sup>24</sup></span><span
style="font-size:13.0pt;
font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"></span>

<span
style="font-size:8.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"> </span>

<span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;">This
subtle obstacle was a matter of special attention in Buddhism,
especially Ch'an. For example, a text with a similar title
(*Hsin*</span><span style="font-size:14.0pt;
font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"> *Ming*</span><span
style="font-size:14.0pt;
font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;">)*,* </span><span
style="font-size:14.0pt;
font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;">attributed to
Fa-jung</span><span
style="font-size:11.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;">
<sup>ay</sup></span><span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;">,</span><span
style="font-size:10.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"><sup>25</sup></span><span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;">
besides other points in common with the *Hsin‑hsin Ming*</span><span
style="font-size:14.0pt;
font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;">, has an admonition similar to
stanza 21. </span><span
style="font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;">\[</span><span
style="font-size:11.0pt;
font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"><sup>ay</sup></span><span
style="font-family:
&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"> </span><span lang="JA"
style="font-family:Osaka\2212\7B49\5E45;
mso-fareast-language:JA">法融<span
style="color:black">、</span>心銘</span><span
style="font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;">\]</span><span
style="font-size:14.0pt;
font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"></span>

<span
style="font-size:8.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"> </span>

<span
style="font-size:13.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"><span
style="mso-tab-count:
3">                                    </span>*If you wish to attain
purity of mind,*</span><span style="font-size:13.0pt;
font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"></span>

<span
style="font-size:13.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"><span
style="mso-tab-count:
3">                                    </span>*then make effort (in the
context of) no‑mind (...)*</span><span
style="font-size:13.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"></span>

<span
style="font-size:13.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"><span
style="mso-tab-count:
3">                                    </span>*To maintain tranquillity
with the mind is*</span><span style="font-size:13.0pt;
font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"></span>

<span
style="font-size:13.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"><span
style="mso-tab-count:
3">                                    </span>*still not to transcend
the illness (of ignorance)".*</span><span
style="font-size:10.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"><sup>26</sup></span><span
style="font-size:13.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"></span>

<span
style="font-size:8.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"> </span>

<span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;">It is
worth mentioning that in *Hsin‑hsin Ming* </span><span
style="font-size:14.0pt;
font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;">we do not find one of the
common technical terms of Ch'an—especially of the Southern
school—namely, *wu‑hsin*</span><span
style="font-size:11.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"><sup>az</sup></span><span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;">
</span><span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;">(no-mind)*.*
</span><span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;">The
author of our text had much more affinity for one‑mind
(*i-hsin*</span><span
style="font-size:11.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"><sup>ba</sup></span><span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;">), and
*wu‑wei*</span><span
style="font-size:11.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"><sup>bb</sup></span><span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;">
(non‑action – in stanza 20), which is part of the Taoist legacy ("no
mind", which is found in stanza 12, is actually *pu‑hsin*</span><span
style="font-size:11.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"><sup>bc</sup></span><span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;">). With
respect to the Taoist legacy we should say that besides the general
influence felt in part I of the poem, it is also present in using the
typical Taoist term: non‑action (*wu‑wei*</span><span
style="font-size:11.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"><sup>bb</sup></span><span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;">). We
also find *tzu‑jan*</span><span
style="font-size:11.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"><sup>bd</sup></span><span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;">
</span><span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;">(spontaneity)
in stanza 17 (which has a completely Taoist meaning), and in stanza 25.
This is in line with the Ch'an principle, developed under the Taoist
influence – to stress spontaneity, at the expense of rules, or
discipline. </span><span
style="font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;">\[</span><span
style="font-size:11.0pt;
font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"><sup>az</sup></span><span
style="font-family:
&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"> </span><span lang="JA"
style="font-family:Osaka\2212\7B49\5E45;
mso-fareast-language:JA">無心</span><span
style="font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;
mso-fareast-language:JA"><span style="mso-spacerun: yes">  
</span></span><span
style="font-size:11.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"><sup>ba</sup></span><span
style="font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;mso-fareast-language:JA">
</span><span lang="JA"
style="font-family:Osaka\2212\7B49\5E45;mso-fareast-language:JA">一心</span><span
style="font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;color:black;mso-fareast-language:JA"><span
style="mso-spacerun: yes">   </span></span><span style="font-size:
11.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"><sup>bb</sup></span><span
style="font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;color:black;mso-fareast-language:JA">
</span><span lang="JA"
style="font-family:Osaka\2212\7B49\5E45;color:black;mso-fareast-language:
JA">無</span><span
style="font-family:Osaka\2212\7B49\5E45;color:black">爲</span><span
style="font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;mso-fareast-language:JA"><span
style="mso-spacerun: yes">   </span></span><span style="font-size:
11.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"><sup>bc</sup></span><span
style="font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;mso-fareast-language:JA">
</span><span lang="JA"
style="font-family:Osaka\2212\7B49\5E45;mso-fareast-language:JA">不心</span><span
style="font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;mso-fareast-language:JA"><span
style="mso-spacerun: yes">   </span></span><span style="font-size:
11.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"><sup>bd</sup></span><span
style="font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;color:black;mso-fareast-language:JA">
</span><span lang="JA"
style="font-family:Osaka\2212\7B49\5E45;mso-fareast-language:JA">自然</span><span
style="font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;">\]</span><span
style="font-size:14.0pt;
font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"></span>

<span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"><span
style="mso-tab-count:
1">         </span>In *Hsin‑hsin Ming*</span><span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"> we
cannot find any trace of the debate between the concepts of gradual and
sudden awakening. We know that the concept of sudden awakening was
already present in Indian Buddhism – "one-moment"
(*eka-kshana*</span><span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;">)
awakening. However it seems that this concept was not concurrent, or
opposed, to the idea of gradualness in Indian Buddhism.</span><span
style="font-size:10.0pt;font-family:
&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"><sup>27</sup></span><span
style="font-size:14.0pt;
font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"> In China the debate lasted
several centuries – from the beginning of the fifth, until the end of
the eighth century, with certain lapses. It started before Ch'an was
recognized as a separate school but was most fervently pursued in Ch'an,
especially after the division between the Northern and the Southern
schools.</span>

<span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"><span
style="mso-tab-count:
1">         </span>The first person in Ch'an who confronted sudden with
gradual awakening, was Tao‑sheng</span><span
style="font-size:11.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"><sup>be</sup></span><span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"> (ca.
360‑434).</span><span
style="font-size:10.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"><sup>28</sup></span><span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"> This
aroused the opposition of Hui‑kuan</span><span
style="font-size:11.0pt;font-family:
&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"><sup>bf</sup></span><span
style="font-size:14.0pt;
font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;">, who, like Tao‑sheng, was also
a disciple of Kumarajiva. The debate continued through the fifth
century. We will skip over the fine arguments of this debate and pay
attention to only one remark, relevant for our inquiry. That is the
difference between faith and understanding, in terms of "gradual" and
"sudden". One of the arguments in favor of the doctrine of sudden
awakening was as follows: "Enlightenment (*ming*</span><span
style="font-size:11.0pt;
font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"><sup>bg</sup></span><span
style="font-size:14.0pt;
font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;">) is not to be gradually
reached, whereas faith (*hsin*</span><span
style="font-size:11.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"><sup>bh</sup></span><span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;">)
arises (gradually) from instruction. What do I mean by this? Faith
arises and is strengthened in daily progress, but enlightenment is not
gradual" (*The Discussion of Essentials*</span><span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;">).</span><span
style="font-size:10.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"><sup>29</sup></span><span
style="font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"> \[</span><span
style="font-size:11.0pt;
font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"><sup>be</sup></span><span
style="font-family:
&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"> </span><span lang="JA"
style="font-family:Osaka\2212\7B49\5E45;
mso-fareast-language:JA">道生</span><span
style="font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;
mso-fareast-language:JA"><span style="mso-spacerun: yes">  
</span></span><span
style="font-size:11.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"><sup>bf</sup></span><span
style="font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;mso-fareast-language:JA">
</span><span lang="JA"
style="font-family:Osaka\2212\7B49\5E45;mso-fareast-language:JA">慧觀</span><span
style="font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;color:black;mso-fareast-language:JA"><span
style="mso-spacerun: yes">   </span></span><span style="font-size:
11.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"><sup>bg</sup></span><span
style="font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;color:black;mso-fareast-language:JA">
</span><span lang="JA"
style="font-family:Osaka\2212\7B49\5E45;mso-fareast-language:JA">明</span><span
style="font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;mso-fareast-language:JA"><span
style="mso-spacerun: yes">   </span></span><span style="font-size:
11.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"><sup>bh</sup></span><span
style="font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;mso-fareast-language:JA">
</span><span lang="JA"
style="font-family:Osaka\2212\7B49\5E45;mso-fareast-language:JA">信</span><span
style="font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;">\]</span><span
style="font-size:14.0pt;
font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"></span>

<span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"><span
style="mso-tab-count:
1">         </span>The fundamental and obvious argument in favor of
suddenness is that the awakening is one: non‑dual and non‑divisible.
This would mean that faith‑in‑mind (*hsin‑hsin*</span><span
style="font-size:11.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"><sup>bi</sup></span><span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;">),
appearing in stanza 36 as non‑dual, is not the same as divisible (and
gradual) faith mentioned in this debate (the character *hsin is*
</span><span style="font-size:
14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;">the same). *Hsin‑hsin
Ming*</span><span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;">
mentions neither sudden awakening (*tun‑wu*</span><span
style="font-size:11.0pt;font-family:
&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"><sup>bj</sup></span><span
style="font-size:14.0pt;
font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;">), nor gradual awakening
(*chien‑wu*</span><span
style="font-size:11.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"><sup>bk</sup></span><span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;">),
which were already in use at the time of Tao‑sheng (i.e. three centuries
before the supposed time of *Hsin‑hsin Ming*</span><span
style="font-size:14.0pt;
font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;">). Its author deemed as
unnecessary to specify (in terms of gradual or sudden) complete
awakenness (*cheng‑chüeh*</span><span
style="font-size:11.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"><sup>bl</sup></span><span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;">), and
awakening (*wu*</span><span
style="font-size:11.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"><sup>bm</sup></span><span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;">).
</span><span
style="font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;">\[</span><span
style="font-size:11.0pt;
font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"><sup>bi</sup></span><span
style="font-family:
&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"> </span><span lang="JA"
style="font-family:Osaka\2212\7B49\5E45;
mso-fareast-language:JA">信心</span><span
style="font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;
mso-fareast-language:JA"><span style="mso-spacerun: yes">  
</span></span><span
style="font-size:11.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"><sup>bj</sup></span><span
style="font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;mso-fareast-language:JA">
</span><span lang="JA"
style="font-family:Osaka\2212\7B49\5E45;mso-fareast-language:JA">頓悟</span><span
style="font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;color:black;mso-fareast-language:JA"><span
style="mso-spacerun: yes">   </span></span><span style="font-size:
11.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"><sup>bk</sup></span><span
style="font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;mso-fareast-language:JA">
</span><span lang="JA"
style="font-family:Osaka\2212\7B49\5E45;mso-fareast-language:JA">漸悟</span><span
style="font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;mso-fareast-language:JA"><span
style="mso-spacerun: yes">   </span></span><span style="font-size:
11.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"><sup>bl</sup></span><span
style="font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;mso-fareast-language:JA">
</span><span lang="JA"
style="font-family:Osaka\2212\7B49\5E45;mso-fareast-language:JA">正覺</span><span
style="font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;mso-fareast-language:JA"><span
style="mso-spacerun: yes">   </span></span><span style="font-size:
11.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"><sup>bm</sup></span><span
style="font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;mso-fareast-language:JA">
</span><span lang="JA"
style="font-family:Osaka\2212\7B49\5E45;mso-fareast-language:JA">悟</span><span
style="font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;">\]</span><span
style="font-size:14.0pt;
font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"></span>

<span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"><span
style="mso-tab-count:
1">         </span>The sixth century was an intermezzo. In the seventh
century the debate between the doctrines of gradual and sudden awakening
burst with new strength in an encounter between Shen‑hsiu</span><span
style="font-size:11.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"><sup>bn</sup></span><span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"> and
Hui‑neng</span><span
style="font-size:11.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"><sup>bo</sup></span><span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;">, and
in the division of Ch'an (into Northern and Southern sects).
</span><span
style="font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;">\[</span><span
style="font-size:11.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"><sup>bn</sup></span><span
style="font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"> </span><span lang="JA"
style="font-family:
Osaka\2212\7B49\5E45;mso-fareast-language:JA">神秀</span><span
style="font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;mso-fareast-language:JA"><span
style="mso-spacerun: yes">   </span></span><span style="font-size:
11.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"><sup>bo</sup></span><span
style="font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;mso-fareast-language:JA">
</span><span lang="JA"
style="font-family:Osaka\2212\7B49\5E45;mso-fareast-language:JA">慧能</span><span
style="font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;color:black;mso-fareast-language:JA">\]</span><span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"></span>

<span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"><span
style="mso-tab-count:
1">         </span>By the end of the eighth century, in 794 A.D., there
was also a recorded debate on the international level (held in Tibet),
between Kamalasila from India, who was representing the orthodox gradual
doctrine, and the exponents of Ch'an from China, who argued in favor of
the doctrine of sudden enlightenment.</span><span
style="font-size:10.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"><sup>30</sup></span><span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"></span>

<span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"><span
style="mso-tab-count:
1">         </span>It should be noted that in *Hsin‑hsin
Ming*</span><span style="font-size:14.0pt;
font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"> we </span><span
style="font-size:14.0pt;
font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;">find altogether two terms
related with awakening – *cheng-chüeh*</span><span
style="font-size:11.0pt;font-family:
&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"><sup>bp</sup></span><span
style="font-size:14.0pt;
font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"> (stanza 19) and
*wu*</span><span
style="font-size:11.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"><sup>bq</sup></span><span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;">
(stanza 21). In Chinese Buddhism *ming*</span><span
style="font-size:11.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"><sup>br</sup></span><span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;">
(enlightenment) was used at least from the time of Tao‑sheng (c. 400
A.D.), as a synonym for *wu*</span><span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;">. This
means that during the Indian history of Buddhism the basic term was
"awakening" (Skt. *bodhi*</span><span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;">), and
that Chinese Buddhism introduced the term "enlightenment"
(*ming*</span><span
style="font-size:11.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"><sup>br</sup></span><span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;">)</span><span
style="font-size:10.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"><sup>31</sup></span><span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"> into
Buddhism (one should not be confused with the fact that, for separate
reasons, in western writings the term "enlightenment" was used more
often – it is more popular – then "awakening"). We also encounter this
character (*ming*</span><span
style="font-size:11.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"><sup>br</sup></span><span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;">) in
*Hsin‑hsin Ming*</span><span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;">,
although not in a noun‑sense (enlightenment). In stanza 1 (fourth line)
it is used as a verb (enlighten), and in stanza 29 as an attribute
(enlightened) – "ming"</span><span style="font-size:11.0pt;
font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"> <sup>bs</sup></span><span
style="font-size:
14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"> appearing in the tittle
of the text is a different character, which means "inscription."
</span><span
style="font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;">\[</span><span
style="font-size:11.0pt;
font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"><sup>bp</sup></span><span
style="font-family:
&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"> </span><span lang="JA"
style="font-family:Osaka\2212\7B49\5E45;
mso-fareast-language:JA">正覺</span><span
style="font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;
mso-fareast-language:JA"><span style="mso-spacerun: yes">  
</span></span><span
style="font-size:11.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"><sup>bq</sup></span><span
style="font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;mso-fareast-language:JA">
</span><span lang="JA"
style="font-family:Osaka\2212\7B49\5E45;mso-fareast-language:JA">悟</span><span
style="font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;color:black;mso-fareast-language:JA"><span
style="mso-spacerun: yes">   </span></span><span style="font-size:
11.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"><sup>br</sup></span><span
style="font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;color:black;mso-fareast-language:JA">
</span><span lang="JA"
style="font-family:Osaka\2212\7B49\5E45;mso-fareast-language:JA">明</span><span
style="font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;mso-fareast-language:JA"><span
style="mso-spacerun: yes">   </span></span><span style="font-size:
11.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"><sup>bs</sup></span><span
style="font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;mso-fareast-language:JA">
</span><span lang="JA"
style="font-family:Osaka\2212\7B49\5E45;mso-fareast-language:JA">銘</span><span
style="font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;">\]</span>

<span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"><span
style="mso-tab-count:
1">         </span>*Chüeh*</span><span
style="font-size:11.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"><sup>bt</sup></span><span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"> means
"to awaken," "completely understand", or "awakenness" as a permanent
accomplishment, while *wu*</span><span style="font-size:11.0pt;
font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"><sup>bu</sup></span><span
style="font-size:14.0pt;
font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"> means "awakening". It is
obvious that these two were used as technical terms –
*cheng‑chüeh*</span><span
style="font-size:11.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"><sup>bv</sup></span><span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;">
meaning "perfect awakenness" (Skt. *sambodhi),* </span><span
style="font-size:14.0pt;
font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;">and *wu*</span><span
style="font-size:14.0pt;
font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;">, meaning "awakening"
*(bodhi).* </span><span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;">Concerning
these matters, Garma C.C. Chang remarks that wu "as shown in the Zen
tradition, to denote the inner experience of the awakening to the
*prajna*</span><span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;">‑truth
(the truth realized through transcendental wisdom), is not the same as
that of *cheng‑teng‑chüeh*</span><span
style="font-size:11.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"><sup>bw</sup></span><span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"> (Skt.
*samyaksambodhi*</span><span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;">),
</span><span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;">which
is the final and perfect Enlightenment of Buddhahood. Ch'an Buddhists
seldom talk of *cheng‑chüeh (sambodhi),* </span><span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;">or
speak of their Ch'an experience as *chüeh (bodhi).* </span><span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;">Although
*chüeh*</span><span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"> and
*wu*</span><span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"> are
very </span><span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;">close,
a </span><span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;">difference
still exists between them. *Wu*</span><span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"> refers
more to the awakening experience in its immediate sense, while
*chüeh*</span><span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;">
denotes permanent and complete Enlightenment (...). However, these
experiences are different only in degree of profundity, not in essence,
or in basic principle".</span><span
style="font-size:10.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"><sup>32</sup></span><span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;">
</span><span
style="font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;">\[</span><span
style="font-size:11.0pt;
font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"><sup>bt</sup></span><span
style="font-family:
&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"> </span><span lang="JA"
style="font-family:Osaka\2212\7B49\5E45;
mso-fareast-language:JA">覺</span><span
style="font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;
mso-fareast-language:JA"><span style="mso-spacerun: yes">  
</span></span><span
style="font-size:11.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"><sup>bu</sup></span><span
style="font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;mso-fareast-language:JA">
</span><span lang="JA"
style="font-family:Osaka\2212\7B49\5E45;mso-fareast-language:JA">悟</span><span
style="font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;color:black;mso-fareast-language:JA"><span
style="mso-spacerun: yes">   </span></span><span style="font-size:
11.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"><sup>bv</sup></span><span
style="font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;color:black;mso-fareast-language:JA">
</span><span lang="JA"
style="font-family:Osaka\2212\7B49\5E45;mso-fareast-language:JA">正覺</span><span
style="font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;mso-fareast-language:JA"><span
style="mso-spacerun: yes">   </span></span><span style="font-size:
11.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"><sup>bw</sup></span><span
style="font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;mso-fareast-language:JA">
</span><span lang="JA"
style="font-family:Osaka\2212\7B49\5E45;mso-fareast-language:JA">正等覺</span><span
style="font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;">\]</span><span
style="font-size:14.0pt;
font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"></span>

<span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"><span
style="mso-tab-count:
1">         </span>It is also worth noting that in
Hsuan‑tsang's</span><span style="font-size:11.0pt;
font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"><sup>bx</sup></span><span
style="font-size:14.0pt;
font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"> doctrine of Mere Ideation
(seventh century), in Fa‑tsang's Hua‑yen, and in T'ien‑t'ai we find
*chüeh* </span><span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;">rather
than *wu*</span><span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;">.</span><span
style="font-size:10.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"><sup>33</sup></span><span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;">
</span><span
style="font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;">\[</span><span
style="font-size:11.0pt;
font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"><sup>bx</sup></span><span
style="font-family:
&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"> </span><span lang="JA"
style="font-family:Osaka\2212\7B49\5E45;
mso-fareast-language:JA">玄奘</span><span
style="font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;
mso-fareast-language:JA">\]</span><span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:
&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"></span>

<span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"> </span>

<span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;">**VI**</span><span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"></span>

<span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;">In
stanza 24 we encounter two important terms—one suchness
(*i‑ju*</span><span
style="font-size:11.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"><sup>by</sup></span><span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;">) and
conditions (*yüan*</span><span
style="font-size:11.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"><sup>bz</sup></span><span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;">). We
have already mentioned the second term, which is also found in stanza 5
with the same meaning (Skt. *pratyaya*</span><span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:
&quot;Times New Roman&quot;">; Pali, *paccaya*</span><span
style="font-size:14.0pt;
font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"> — root‑conditions: greed,
hate, delusion, etc.). Concerning suchness, we find altogether three
variations of this term in *Hsin‑hsin Ming*</span><span
style="font-size:14.0pt;
font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;">. In stanza 4 we find
"suchness" (*ju*</span><span
style="font-size:11.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"><sup>ca</sup></span><span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;">), in
stanza 24 "one suchness", and in stanza 30 "real suchness"
(*chen‑ju*</span><span
style="font-size:11.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"><sup>cb</sup></span><span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;color:black;mso-fareast-language:
JA"> </span><span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;">– Skt.
*bhutatathata*</span><span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;">). The
first and the third are well known in Mahayana tradition, but the second
seems to be an innovation of the author of *Hsin‑hsin Ming*</span><span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;">.
</span><span
style="font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;">\[</span><span
style="font-size:11.0pt;
font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"><sup>by</sup></span><span
style="font-family:
&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"> </span><span lang="JA"
style="font-family:Osaka\2212\7B49\5E45;
mso-fareast-language:JA">一如</span><span lang="JA" style="font-family:
&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"> </span><span
style="font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;
mso-fareast-language:JA"><span
style="mso-spacerun: yes">  </span></span><span
style="font-size:11.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"><sup>bz</sup></span><span
style="font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;mso-fareast-language:JA">
</span><span lang="JA"
style="font-family:Osaka\2212\7B49\5E45;color:black;mso-fareast-language:
JA">縁</span><span
style="font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;mso-fareast-language:
JA"><span style="mso-spacerun: yes">   </span></span><span
style="font-size:11.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"><sup>ca</sup></span><span
style="font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;mso-fareast-language:JA">
</span><span lang="JA"
style="font-family:Osaka\2212\7B49\5E45;mso-fareast-language:JA">如</span><span
style="font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;mso-fareast-language:JA"><span
style="mso-spacerun: yes">   </span></span><span style="font-size:
11.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"><sup>cb</sup></span><span
style="font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;mso-fareast-language:JA">
</span><span lang="JA"
style="font-family:Osaka\2212\7B49\5E45;color:black;mso-fareast-language:
JA">眞</span><span
style="font-family:Osaka\2212\7B49\5E45;color:black">如</span><span
style="font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;">\]</span><span
style="font-size:14.0pt;
font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"></span>

<span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"> </span>

<span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;">**VII**</span><span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"></span>

<span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;">Stanzas
28‑29 can be compared with Seng‑chao: "Sage harbors (no desires, his
mind is like an) empty hole: there are no perceptions nor thoughts.
Indeed, though living in the midst of our ever‑changing world, he
remains completely detached..."</span><span
style="font-size:10.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;">
<sup>34</sup></span><span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"></span>

<span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"><span
style="mso-tab-count:
1">         </span>In the first line of stanza 30 we find two technical
terms: real suchness (*chen‑ju*</span><span
style="font-size:11.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"><sup>cc</sup></span><span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;">), and
thing‑realm, or totality of dharmas, *fa chieh*</span><span
style="font-size:11.0pt;
font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"><sup>cd</sup></span><span
style="font-size:14.0pt;
font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"> (Skt. *dharma-dhatu).*
</span><span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;">These
concepts have been used in Mahayana, and also in the Mind‑only school,
T'ien‑t'ai, and Hua‑yen. In *Ch'eng Wei‑shih Lun* </span><span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;">Hsuan‑tsang
gives the following definitions. "*Chen*</span><span
style="font-size:11.0pt;
font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"><sup>ce</sup></span><span
style="font-size:14.0pt;
font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"> means genuine and real. It
indicates that it is not baseless and false. *Ju*</span><span
style="font-size:11.0pt;
font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"><sup>cf</sup></span><span
style="font-size:14.0pt;
font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"> means constantly thus. The
meaning is that this genuine reality remains, under all conditions,
constantly thus in its nature".</span><span
style="font-size:10.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"><sup>35</sup></span><span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;">
</span><span
style="font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;">\[</span><span
style="font-size:11.0pt;
font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"><sup>cc</sup></span><span
style="font-family:
&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"> </span><span lang="JA"
style="font-family:Osaka\2212\7B49\5E45;
color:black;mso-fareast-language:JA">眞</span><span style="font-family:
Osaka\2212\7B49\5E45;color:black">如</span><span
style="font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;
mso-fareast-language:JA"><span style="mso-spacerun: yes">  
</span></span><span
style="font-size:11.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"><sup>cd</sup></span><span
style="font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;mso-fareast-language:JA">
</span><span lang="JA"
style="font-family:Osaka\2212\7B49\5E45;color:black;mso-fareast-language:
JA">法界</span><span style="font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;
color:black;mso-fareast-language:JA"><span style="mso-spacerun:
yes">   </span></span><span
style="font-size:11.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"><sup>ce</sup></span><span
style="font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;color:black;mso-fareast-language:JA">
</span><span lang="JA"
style="font-family:Osaka\2212\7B49\5E45;color:black;mso-fareast-language:
JA">眞</span><span
style="font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;mso-fareast-language:
JA"><span style="mso-spacerun: yes">   </span></span><span
style="font-size:11.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"><sup>cf</sup></span><span
style="font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;mso-fareast-language:JA">
</span><span lang="JA"
style="font-family:Osaka\2212\7B49\5E45;mso-fareast-language:JA">如</span><span
style="font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;mso-fareast-language:JA">\]</span><span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;mso-fareast-language:
JA"></span>

<span
style="font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;mso-fareast-language:JA"><span
style="mso-tab-count:1">            </span></span><span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;">The
T'ien‑t'ai school gives a slightly different meaning: "Further as to
*chen‑ju:* </span><span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;">it is
that of all things which, being genuinely and really thus, consists of
the single mind only. This single mind is therefore called
*chen‑ju*</span><span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;">
(genuinely thus). Anything external to it is neither genuine nor thus,:
but consists only of false and: diverse appearances".</span><span
style="font-size:10.0pt;
font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"><sup>36</sup></span><span
style="font-size:14.0pt;
font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"> </span><span
style="font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;">\[</span><span
style="font-size:11.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"><sup>cg</sup></span><span
style="font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"> </span><span lang="JA"
style="font-family:
Osaka\2212\7B49\5E45;color:black;mso-fareast-language:JA">眞</span><span
style="font-family:Osaka\2212\7B49\5E45;color:black">如</span><span
style="font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;color:black">\]</span><span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"></span>

<span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"><span
style="mso-tab-count:
1">         </span>In stanza 30 and the first two lines of stanza 31, we
find the relation between real suchness (*chen‑ju*</span><span
style="font-size:11.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"><sup>ch</sup></span><span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;">),
</span><span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;">non‑duality
(*pu‑erh*</span><span
style="font-size:11.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"><sup>ci</sup></span><span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;">),
equality (*t'ung*</span><span
style="font-size:11.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"><sup>cj</sup></span><span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;">),</span><span
style="font-size:10.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"><sup>37</sup></span><span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"> and
totality (nothing is left out) of the thing (*dharma*</span><span
style="font-size:11.0pt;
font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"><sup>ck</sup></span><span
style="font-size:14.0pt;
font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;">) realm (*fa*</span><span
style="font-size:
14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"> *chieh*</span><span
style="font-size:11.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"><sup>cl</sup></span><span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;">). The
connecting experience between the "meditative" (*dhyana*</span><span
style="font-size:
14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;">) and "wisdom"
(*prajna*</span><span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;">)
aspects is the negation of the difference between "other"
(*t'a*</span><span
style="font-size:11.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"><sup>cm</sup></span><span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;">) and
"self" (*tzu*</span><span
style="font-size:11.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"><sup>cn</sup></span><span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;">). In
meditation this is the experience of non‑obstruction between ego and
non‑ego, when "all is free of marks" – and therefore, "not-different"
(in a Buddhist context it would not be consistent to say that the ego
has become all‑inclusive with the falling off of the ego boundaries,
because ego is also without marks). In the "wisdom" sense this means
that in real suchness it is not possible to make any distinction –
therefore, the realm of things (*fa chieh*</span><span
style="font-size:11.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"><sup>cl</sup></span><span
style="font-size:14.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;">),
where nothing is left out, is experienced as non‑distinctive totality,
or oneness. This can remind someone of postmodern debate on
"difference", and "other", but this is a different context, and should
not be meddled with postmodern debate. </span><span
style="font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;">\[</span><span
style="font-size:11.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"><sup>ch</sup></span><span
style="font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"> </span><span lang="JA"
style="font-family:
Osaka\2212\7B49\5E45;color:black;mso-fareast-language:JA">眞</span><span
style="font-family:Osaka\2212\7B49\5E45;color:black">如</span><span
style="font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;mso-fareast-language:JA"><span
style="mso-spacerun: yes">   </span></span><span style="font-size:
11.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"><sup>ci</sup></span><span
style="font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;mso-fareast-language:JA">
</span><span lang="JA"
style="font-family:Osaka\2212\7B49\5E45;color:black;mso-fareast-language:
JA">不二</span><span style="font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;
color:black;mso-fareast-language:JA"><span style="mso-spacerun:
yes">   </span></span><span
style="font-size:11.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"><sup>cj</sup></span><span
style="font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;color:black;mso-fareast-language:JA">
</span><span lang="JA"
style="font-family:Osaka\2212\7B49\5E45;color:black;mso-fareast-language:
JA">同</span><span
style="font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;mso-fareast-language:
JA"><span style="mso-spacerun: yes">   </span></span><span
style="font-size:11.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"><sup>ck</sup></span><span
style="font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;mso-fareast-language:JA">
</span><span lang="JA"
style="font-family:Osaka\2212\7B49\5E45;color:black;mso-fareast-language:
JA">法</span><span
style="font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;color:black"><span
style="mso-spacerun: yes">   </span></span><span style="font-size:
11.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;"><sup>cl</sup></span><span
style="font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;mso-fareast-language:JA">
</span><span lang="JA"
style="font-family:Osaka\2212\7B49\5E45;color:black;mso-fareast-language:
JA">法界</span><span style="font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;
color:black"><span style="mso-spacerun: yes">   </span></span><span
